    "type": "blogs",
    "title": "Leigh Barnard Wants More Women In Supply Chain™",
    "slug": "leigh-barnard-wants-more-women-in-supply-chain",
    "date": "2026-01-20T22:22:11",
    "summary": null,
    "main_points": null,
    "recent_news": null,
    "related_articles": [],
    "web_content": "<p>Welcome to 2026—it’s a new year, ripe with tremendous disruption and opportunities that have been the hallmark of the 2020’s so far. Gender diversity is more important than ever for companies to navigate the latest sea changes and drive business success. Why? Businesses with women on their executive committees earn a return on equity almost 50% higher than those without. Organizations in the top 25% for gender diversity are 27% more likely to outperform the industry average in profitability.</p>\r\n<p>While women are rising in the ranks—up to 29% in the C-suite, up from 17% a decade earlier—men still hold 66% of management roles. And women still receive less advocacy and sponsorship, meaning fewer promotions and less representation at the top.</p>\r\n<p>But there’s good news, too: <a href=\"https://www.ismworld.org/supply-management-news-and-reports/news-publications/inside-supply-management-magazine/blog/2024/2024-093/womens-representation-in-supply-chain-survey-finds-mixed-results/\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\">recent reports</a> show that women now make up 40% of the supply chain workforce. At Let’s Talk Supply Chain, our Women In Supply Chain™ series aims to increase that number and expand mentorship, career growth, and advancement opportunities for women who are as qualified as their male counterparts.</p>\r\n<p>Our Let’s Talk Supply Chain <a href=\"https://letstalksupplychain.com/women-in-supply-chain/\">Women In Supply Chain™ program</a>, blog, and podcast series showcase the importance of greater gender representation. This month’s featured leader is an outspoken advocate for women entering the industry and advancing in their careers.</p>\r\n<p>We are honored to highlight <a href=\"https://www.linkedin.com/in/leigh-barnard-4b7a7415/\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\">Leigh Barnard</a>, the Chief Operating Officer at Cooler Logistics. Leigh boasts 15 years of experience in leading operational growth strategies for supply chain organizations and building critical relationships with customers, shippers, and receivers. She has a Master&#8217;s in Library and Information Science from the University of Illinois Urbana-Champaign and a Bachelor of Arts in Public Relations and Advertising from DePaul University.</p>\r\n<h4><span style=\"font-size: 1.7em;\">1. How did your supply chain journey start?</span></h4>\r\n<p>I never intended for logistics to be my career. I majored in PR and Advertising, but graduated at a time when there were fewer opportunities in those fields. After dozens of rejected applications, I realized I needed to shift gears. Load Delivered took a chance on me and brought me on in an entry operations role. It didn’t take long for me to realize that this fast-paced industry, which rewarded drive and celebrated innovation, was where I was meant to be. I transitioned from operations to account management, eventually working my way up to senior management, and now serve as the COO of Cooler Logistics. Every role has taught me more about myself and reinforced the fact that logistics is where I was always meant to be.</p>\r\n<h2>2. How have mentors played a role in your growth as a woman in supply chain?</h2>\r\n<p>I’ve learned a lot from so many people throughout my career, but I don’t have anyone I would label a mentor. That’s one of the reasons I was drawn to Let’s Talk Supply Chain’s Woman In Supply Chain series. This industry would benefit from creating and growing a mentor pipeline.</p>\r\n<h2>3. What’s your experience working in a male-dominated industry?</h2>\r\n<p>Working in a historically male-dominated industry has been an incredible experience. Knowing that your voice is underrepresented makes you more intentional about how you use it. When I’m at the table with leadership, I understand that I’m setting the tone and expectations for those who come after me. While that can be a lot of pressure, it’s a powerful opportunity to stand out.</p>\r\n<h2>4. When did you find your voice in your career?</h2>\r\n<p>Like many young professionals early in their careers, I thought the best way to be heard was to have an opinion about everything. I gave feedback, requested or not, on every process change, technology rollout, and policy adjustment. My manager at the time pulled me aside and told me I needed to do a better job of picking my battles. While that felt harsh initially, I took it to heart. I realized that being more strategic about when and how I used my voice significantly increased its impact and allowed me to influence real change within my departments.</p>\r\n<h2>5. What advice do you have for Women In Supply Chain™ and others looking to start a career in the industry?</h2>\r\n<p>Don’t give up your voice for the sake of likability. Women are taught from a very young age that likeability is king. We want to please our parents, get along with our friends, and be admired by our teachers. This ingrained need can, in some ways, be a strength—our high social and emotional intelligence helps us navigate high-stress situations with ease. But people-pleasing can quickly become a weakness if it leads you to silence your ideas and opinions to avoid confrontation. Be respectful, but make your voice heard. There are still people in this world who label an outspoken woman a hassle, but far more don’t, and they will have your back if you dare to speak up.</p>\r\n<h2>6. Who do you admire in and outside of the supply chain?</h2>\r\n<p>I really admire Melinda Gates. She’s a shining example of how wealth and philanthropy should go hand in hand, and how true success cannot be achieved without giving back to our communities. Gates’ philanthropic focus can and should be replicated across all industries. Her dedication to women’s health and education is incredibly inspiring.</p>\r\n<h2>7. What have you learned on your supply chain journey so far and what’s next?</h2>\r\n<p>I’ve learned that I want to be great at my job. I want the people I work with to know that I will show up every day and put in 100%. On the flip side, I know I won’t be happy working with people who don’t show up in the same way. The future holds more opportunities to gain experience as a leader, and I intend to seize them. A year from now, I hope I’ve pushed to hire more women at <a href=\"http://coolerlogistics.com/\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\">Cooler Logistics</a>, spent time mentoring and coaching each of them, increased our philanthropic efforts by growing our <a href=\"https://www.coolerlogistics.com/about/\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\">Cooler Cares initiative</a>, and spent more time learning about this massive industry and expanding my network.</p>\r\n<h2>8. What does this Women In Supply Chain™ feature mean to you?</h2>\r\n<p>It’s such an honor to be featured in the Woman in Supply Chain series. When I started at my first brokerage, I so desperately wanted a woman mentor to look up to and learn from, so it would be incredibly rewarding to be that person for someone else. The supply chain and logistics industry offers so many opportunities, and I believe that highlighting successful women in logistics will inspire more to enter the field.</p>\r\n<p>&nbsp;</p>\r\n<p><em>We hope our Women In Supply Chain™ blog series inspires readers to reimagine what’s possible, take action, and bring people from different backgrounds together for stronger and more meaningful collaboration. Keep reading our </em><a href=\"https://letstalksupplychain.com/women-in-supply-chain/\"><em>Women In Supply Chain™ Blog</em></a><em>.</em></p>\r\n<h4> </h4>\r\n<h3 dir=\"ltr\">Women In Supply Chain™: Empowering Your Journey at Every Career Stage</h3>\r\n<p dir=\"ltr\">Whether you&#8217;re just starting or leading at the highest levels, our Women In Supply Chain™ membership programs are designed to support you in every career phase. We offer multiple tailored tiers to help you connect, grow, and lead within the supply chain industry.</p>\r\n<p dir=\"ltr\">Women In Supply Chain™ Connections<br />Build Your Network. Shape Your Future. ($199/year)</p>\r\n<p dir=\"ltr\">Step into a vibrant community where you can share, learn, and grow as a woman in supply chain. Whether you&#8217;re just beginning your career or seeking support in your current role, Women In Supply Chain™ Connections provides an essential space to connect, network, and thrive. For $199 a year, you&#8217;ll will:</p>\r\n<p dir=\"ltr\">What you&#8217;ll experience:</p>\r\n<ul>\r\n<li dir=\"ltr\">\r\n<p dir=\"ltr\" role=\"presentation\">Dynamic virtual discussions on pressing industry topics</p>\r\n</li>\r\n<li dir=\"ltr\">\r\n<p dir=\"ltr\" role=\"presentation\">Exclusive access to targeted job opportunities through our community board</p>\r\n</li>\r\n<li dir=\"ltr\">\r\n<p dir=\"ltr\" role=\"presentation\">Meet-ups to build authentic relationships with peers</p>\r\n</li>\r\n<li dir=\"ltr\">\r\n<p dir=\"ltr\" role=\"presentation\">Bi-annual virtual networking events with industry leaders</p>\r\n</li>\r\n<li dir=\"ltr\">\r\n<p dir=\"ltr\" role=\"presentation\">A supportive community that champions your growth</p>\r\n</li>\r\n</ul>\r\n<p dir=\"ltr\">Perfect for: Supply chain professionals seeking to expand their network and tap into a supportive community of like-minded women.</p>\r\n<p dir=\"ltr\">Connect, Collaborate, and Grow with Women In Supply Chain™ Connections</p>\r\n<p dir=\"ltr\">Are you a woman navigating the dynamic world of supply chain? Join our vibrant community and gain access to:</p>\r\n<ul>\r\n<li dir=\"ltr\">\r\n<p dir=\"ltr\" role=\"presentation\">Virtual discussions on relevant topics</p>\r\n</li>\r\n<li dir=\"ltr\">\r\n<p dir=\"ltr\" role=\"presentation\">Community job boards and local meetups</p>\r\n</li>\r\n<li dir=\"ltr\">\r\n<p dir=\"ltr\" role=\"presentation\">Bi-annual virtual networking events</p>\r\n</li>\r\n<li dir=\"ltr\">\r\n<p dir=\"ltr\" role=\"presentation\">And much more!</p>\r\n</li>\r\n</ul>\r\n<p dir=\"ltr\"><em><strong>Join today for just $199 a year!</strong></em></p>\r\n<p dir=\"ltr\"> </p>\r\n<h2><strong>Meet Our Sponsors</strong></h2>\r\n<p>The <a href=\"https://www.womeninsupplychainforum.com/\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\">Women In Supply Chain™ Forum</a>™ was co-created by Marina Mayer, Editor-in-Chief of <i>Food Logistics</i> and <i>Supply &amp; Demand Chain Executive</i>, to bring female logistics professionals together to network, learn, and build lasting bonds beyond traditional conferences. It’s about strengthening pipelines, creating a community of advocates, mentors, and trusted peers and branding yourself, both personally and professionally. Similarly, the Women In Supply Chain™ Award was born from a need to recognize female leaders navigating challenges and driving change. Since its inception five years ago, it has grown to nearly 400 submissions, celebrating the achievements of women shaping the future of supply chain.     "title": "The Great Reshuffling of Shipping Alliances in 2025: What It Means for Global Trade",
    "slug": "the-great-reshuffling-of-shipping-alliances-in-2025-what-it-means-for-global-trade",
    "date": "2025-02-25T01:17:30",
    "summary": null,
    "main_points": null,
    "recent_news": null,
    "related_articles": [],
    "web_content": "<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The global shipping industry is undergoing a massive restructuring in 2025, with long-standing alliances dissolving and new partnerships emerging. These shifts are set to redefine carrier operations, impact freight rates, and change how businesses manage their supply chains.<br />\n<img fetchpriority=\"high\" decoding=\"async\" class=\"alignnone wp-image-27213\" src=\"https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/02/unnamed-300x150.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"706\" height=\"353\" title=\"\" srcset=\"https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/02/unnamed-300x150.png 300w, https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/02/unnamed-1024x512.png 1024w, https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/02/unnamed-768x384.png 768w, https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/02/unnamed-1536x768.png 1536w, https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/02/unnamed-600x300.png 600w, https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/02/unnamed.png 1600w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 706px) 100vw, 706px\" /><br />\n</span></p>\n<h3><b>The End of the 2M Alliance: A New Era for Maersk &amp; MSC</b></h3>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">For nearly a decade, </span><b>the 2M Alliance</b><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">, a strategic vessel-sharing agreement between </span><b>Maersk</b><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> and </span><b>MSC</b><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">, played a dominant role in global container shipping. This collaboration allowed both carriers to optimize network coverage, reduce operational costs, and improve service reliability.</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">However, in </span><b>early 2025, the partnership officially dissolved</b><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">, marking the end of a significant era in ocean freight. This decision was driven by:</span></p>\n<ul>\n<li style=\"font-weight: 400;\" aria-level=\"1\"><b>Diverging Business Strategies</b><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">: Maersk has been shifting towards an integrated logistics model, focusing on end-to-end supply chain solutions, while MSC is doubling down on fleet expansion and independent operations.</span></li>\n<li style=\"font-weight: 400;\" aria-level=\"1\"><b>Market Competition &amp; Regulatory Scrutiny</b><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">: Regulators and market forces have pushed carriers to rethink traditional alliances, prompting a move toward more flexible partnerships.</span></li>\n<li style=\"font-weight: 400;\" aria-level=\"1\"><b>Operational Flexibility</b><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">: Both companies now have greater freedom to tailor their services without being bound by alliance restrictions.</span></li>\n</ul>\n<h3><b>The Birth of the Gemini Cooperation: A New Powerhouse in Shipping</b></h3>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">In response to the 2M breakup, </span><b>Maersk has formed a new partnership with Hapag-Lloyd</b><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">, creating </span><b>the Gemini Cooperation</b><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">. Unlike traditional vessel-sharing agreements, Gemini aims to build a </span><b>more customer-centric and efficient shipping network</b><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">, with key benefits such as:</span></p>\n<ul>\n<li style=\"font-weight: 400;\" aria-level=\"1\"><b>Improved Service Reliability</b><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> – Maersk and Hapag-Lloyd plan to offer enhanced schedule integrity, which has been a major concern for global shippers.</span></li>\n<li style=\"font-weight: 400;\" aria-level=\"1\"><b>Streamlined Port Operations</b><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> – The new network focuses on optimizing port rotations and minimizing congestion.</span></li>\n<li style=\"font-weight: 400;\" aria-level=\"1\"><b>Digitally Integrated Operations</b><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> – Both companies are investing heavily in </span><b>digital freight solutions</b><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">, making cargo tracking and logistics management more seamless for customers.</span></li>\n</ul>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">This move signals a </span><b>more agile and independent future for Maersk</b><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">, aligning with its goal to become a fully integrated logistics provider rather than just a shipping line.</span></p>\n<h3><b>The Ocean Alliance Extension: Strengthening an Existing Giant</b></h3>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">While Maersk and MSC have parted ways, </span><b>other alliances are doubling down on their cooperation</b><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">. The </span><b>Ocean Alliance</b><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">, composed of </span><b>CMA CGM, COSCO Shipping, Evergreen, and OOCL</b><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">, has extended its agreement until </span><b>2032</b><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">.</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">This extension means:</span></p>\n<ul>\n<li style=\"font-weight: 400;\" aria-level=\"1\"><b>Continued Strength in Asia-Europe and Trans-Pacific Trade</b><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> – Ocean Alliance remains a dominant force in these key lanes.</span></li>\n<li style=\"font-weight: 400;\" aria-level=\"1\"><b>Increased Fleet and Service Expansion</b><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> – The members are pooling more vessels and expanding their service portfolios.</span></li>\n<li style=\"font-weight: 400;\" aria-level=\"1\"><b>Greater Market Stability</b><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> – By committing to a long-term partnership, shippers can expect more </span><b>predictable rates and routes</b><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">.</span></li>\n</ul>\n<h3><b>How These Changes Impact Shippers &amp; Supply Chains</b></h3>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">With the </span><b>restructuring of global alliances</b><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">, businesses must </span><b>rethink their ocean freight strategies</b><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">. Here’s what to keep in mind:</span></p>\n<ul>\n<li style=\"font-weight: 400;\" aria-level=\"1\"><b>More Options, but More Complexity</b><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> – As carriers form new partnerships, shippers may need to renegotiate contracts and explore alternative routing options.</span></li>\n<li style=\"font-weight: 400;\" aria-level=\"1\"><b>Potential Freight Rate Volatility</b><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> – The dissolution of the 2M Alliance could lead to short-term rate fluctuations as Maersk and MSC establish independent pricing models.</span></li>\n<li style=\"font-weight: 400;\" aria-level=\"1\"><b>Stronger Focus on Service &amp; Technology</b><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> – The Gemini Cooperation and Ocean Alliance are prioritizing digitalization and efficiency, meaning supply chain managers should </span><b>leverage tech-driven logistics solutions</b><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">.</span></li>\n</ul>\n<p><b>Implications for Shippers</b></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">These alliance shifts have several implications:</span></p>\n<ul>\n<li style=\"font-weight: 400;\" aria-level=\"1\"><b>Contract Negotiations</b><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">: Trans-Pacific carriers are proposing contract rate increases of up to 25% for the 2025–26 period. However, shippers are hesitant to finalize agreements due to uncertainties surrounding tariffs and global trade dynamics. </span>&nbsp;</li>\n<li style=\"font-weight: 400;\" aria-level=\"1\"><b>Market Fluidity</b><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">: The restructuring has led to a dynamic environment where smaller Non-Vessel Operating Common Carriers (NVOCCs) face challenges securing contracts. Many are now collaborating with larger forwarders to ensure space and maintain service levels.</span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><br />\n</span></li>\n</ul>\n<p><b>Strategic Considerations Moving Forward</b></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Given these developments, businesses should:</span></p>\n<ul>\n<li style=\"font-weight: 400;\" aria-level=\"1\"><b>Stay Informed</b><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">: Regularly monitor industry news and alliance announcements to anticipate changes that could impact supply chains.</span></li>\n<li style=\"font-weight: 400;\" aria-level=\"1\"><b>Diversify Partnerships</b><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">: Engage with multiple carriers and forwarders to mitigate risks associated with alliance restructures and rate fluctuations.</span></li>\n<li style=\"font-weight: 400;\" aria-level=\"1\"><b>Adapt Contract Strategies</b><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">: Be prepared for potential rate increases and consider flexible contract terms that allow adjustments based on market conditions.</span></li>\n</ul>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">In this transformative period, proactive and informed strategies are essential for navigating the complexities of global supply chains.</span></p>\n",

    "web_content": "<p> In ⁤the fast-paced world ⁢of‌ aviation,‌ delays are often‍ unavoidable⁤ but ​always ‍impactful.The highly anticipated entry-into-service (EIS) of⁢ the Airbus A350F,originally slated for 2025,now faces ​unexpected hurdles. According⁢ to a report ‍by ch-aviation, supply chain issues have ⁣thrown ⁢a spanner ⁣in ⁢the ⁣works, pushing the EIS of the ‌A350F to 2027. This ⁤setback impacts Airbus&#8217;s timeline and​ stakeholders, raising concerns within the aviation⁤ industry. </p>\n<p>According to sources,the delay⁢ is​ attributed to challenges in the ‍procurement of key ⁤components⁢ for the A350F production,resulting ‍in a ripple effect​ on ⁣the overall ‌manufacturing ‌process. These ‌factors have considerably impacted the timeline for the ‌aircraft&#8217;s entry into service:</p>\n<ul>\n<li><b>Component Shortages:</b> A shortage⁤ of crucial components has‌ slowed down the manufacturing ‌process, leading to⁢ bottlenecks and⁢ delays⁣ in ‍production.</li>\n<li><b>Logistical challenges:</b> ⁢Complications​ in transportation and logistics have hindered the smooth flow of parts and materials, further exacerbating the delay.</li>\n</ul>\n<p>Additionally, fluctuating demand, quality control issues, and‍ unexpected ‌disruptions have ​all played a role in disrupting the supply⁢ chain and causing setbacks in the⁤ delivery schedule.     "web_content": "<h1>Breaking the .XLSX Chains: Corporate Venture Supply Chain Software as the Potential Game-Changer</h1>\n<p>&nbsp;</p>\n<p>From 2018 to 2022, a whopping $55 billion of venture capital poured into supply chain technology. This mammoth investment spawned 27 ‘Unicorn’ companies. Yet, despite the relentless digitalization hype since the mid-2010s, the stronghold of Microsoft Excel remains unbroken. For around the 30th consecutive year, Excel reigns as the most-used Supply Chain Management tool. Multinational Corporations (MNCs) continue to rely on hefty .xlsx files to operate substantial segments of their supply chains. So, what became of this enormous capital injection? Where are the refined solutions that we were promised?</p>\n<p>In the sphere of supply chain technology, particularly in LogTech, an ill-guided narrative emerged. This tale suggested that logistics service providers were severely outdated, and lacking in digitization and transparency. This provocative storyline attracted substantial funding, unfortunately often directed towards founder groups with scant logistics understanding. However, this narrative is fundamentally flawed.</p>\n<p>Logistics service providers have consistently innovated, adapted, and remained at the forefront. They were never the problem. The real issue lies with the MNCs splurging millions on ERP projects, striving to shoehorn their unique supply chain configurations into an outdated, standardized tech set-up hailing from the 90s.</p>\n<p>Trying to fit a dynamic, highly-customized supply chain into a one-size-fits-all tech mold is as futile as trying to squeeze a square peg into a round hole. It’s doomed to fail. The fallout from this mismatch is often thrown at logistics service providers to resolve, leading to disjointed processes managed by trusty .xlsx files.</p>\n<p>So, where do we go from here? Is there a viable solution?</p>\n<p>Yes, and it revolves around acknowledging that supply chain management is far from monolithic. What benefits one corporation may harm another, and what proves effective for one business unit could be detrimental to another. Technology needs to respect this diversity. The venture capital funding should be redirected towards developing adaptable, customizable solutions tailored to cater to a corporation’s specific needs, rather than merely aiming for rapid, unsustainable revenue generation at high churn rates.</p>\n<p>As we chart our course forward, we must understand that digitalization isn’t just a buzzword, but a path toward crafting more efficient, resilient, and customized supply chain solutions. In this context, Corporate Venturing emerges as a potential game-changer. Grounded in real-life experience, solving real-world problems: this approach of devising solutions to everyday challenges has given birth to some exciting products. Examples are no-code tailoring SCM platforms unifying scattered Supply Chain ecosystems, allowing for the customization of supply chain software without draining IT resources.</p>\n<p>By championing solutions developed from hands-on experience and tailored to real-life scenarios, Corporate Venture Supply Chain Software companies can potentially break the chains of .xlsx, leading the way toward a more adaptable, effective, and digitized future for supply chain management.</p>\n<h4>Want to learn more?</h4>\n<p>➡️<a href=\"https://www.logward.com/post/blogpost-digitizing-supply-chains-in-real-life-what-works-and-what-doesnt\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\">  https://www.logward.com/post/blogpost-digitizing-supply-chains-in-real-life-what-works-and-what-doesnt</a></p>\n<p>➡️ <a href=\"https://www.linkedin.com/feed/update/urn:li:activity:6977505206896885760/\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\">https://www.linkedin.com/feed/update/urn:li:activity:6977505206896885760/ </a></p>\n<p>➡️ <a href=\"https://www.logward.com/post/why-your-digitization-campaign-will-fail\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\">https://www.logward.com/post/why-your-digitization-campaign-will-fail </a></p>\n<p>➡️ <a href=\"https://www.logward.com/\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\">https://www.logward.com/</a></p>\n<p>&nbsp;</p>\n<h4><a href=\"https://letstalksupplychain.com/episode-343-create-a-one-stop-solution-for-supply-chain-automation-with-logward/\">Watch the podcast episode where we take a full dive with Logward.     "title": "The Top 5 Challenges for Trucking Companies Providing Container Drayage",
    "slug": "the-top-5-challenges-for-trucking-companies-providing-container-drayage",
    "date": "2023-06-29T06:00:43",
    "summary": null,
    "main_points": null,
    "recent_news": null,
    "related_articles": [],
    "web_content": "<h1>The Top 5 Challenges for Trucking Companies Providing Container Drayage</h1>\n<p>&nbsp;</p>\n<p>Container drayage refers to the transportation of shipping containers by truck between ports, rail yards, and distribution centers. It requires specialized equipment, such as container chassis and heavy-duty trucks, as well as trained drivers who are familiar with the local traffic patterns and regulations.</p>\n<p>Container drayage plays a critical role in the transportation of goods, but it also poses significant challenges for trucking companies. In this blog post, we will explore the top 5 challenges trucking companies face when providing container drayage services.</p>\n<p>1. Dead Runs One of the most significant challenges that trucking companies face when providing container drayage services is dead runs. A dead run is when a trucker has to travel a long distance to pick up or drop off a container but does not have any cargo to transport on the return journey. Dead runs not only waste time and fuel but also reduce profitability for trucking companies.</p>\n<p>Truckers may experience long waiting times at ports or depots when picking up or dropping off containers. They may also encounter situations where they are told to wait for hours, only to be informed that there is no container to pick up or no space to drop off the container. These situations can significantly impact the trucker&#8217;s productivity, leading to longer turnaround times and reduced profitability for the trucking company.</p>\n<p>2. Waiting for Carriers to Release Empty Containers Another significant challenge that trucking companies face is waiting for carriers to release empty containers. Trucking companies have to make a request for an empty container release via email, phone, or fax to the shipping line. The staff at the shipping line then checks their system and responds back to the trucking company with information on where to pick up the empty container.</p>\n<p>This manual process can take an average of 2.5 hours for truckers to receive an empty container release, resulting in delays and inefficiencies in the overall transportation process.</p>\n<p>3. Limited Ability to Choose Pickup Locations Trucking companies often have limited ability to choose pickup locations for containers. When the shipping line provides an empty container release, they inform the trucking company which depot to pick up the container from. The trucking company rarely has a choice in this matter and may have to travel long distances to reach the designated depot.</p>\n<p>There are usually multiple container depots across the city, with varying distances from each other. The lack of choice in selecting the optimal pickup location depending on the trucker&#8217;s schedule for the day can result in delays and increased transportation costs for trucking companies.</p>\n<p>4. Multiple Systems for Bookings and Empty Containers Another significant challenge that trucking companies face is the use of multiple systems to manage bookings and empty containers. With multiple shipping lines, trucking companies have to log in to various systems to input and access information, leading to disorganization and confusion.</p>\n<p>This challenge can result in data discrepancies and manual errors, leading to additional time spent reconciling and updating records across multiple systems.</p>\n<p>5. Limited Time for Drop-offs Trucking companies face a small window of time between early return dates and cut-offs, making it challenging to drop off containers in a timely manner. A missed cut-off can result in additional charges, negatively impacting the profitability of the trucking company.</p>\n<h3>Trakking Helps Solve these 5 Challenges</h3>\n<p>The process of sourcing and managing empty shipping line containers has long been a significant inefficiency for all industries that rely on importing and exporting goods. That&#8217;s why Trakking was launched in 2020 &#8211; a revolutionary digital platform that solves this problem by streamlining the process of requesting, managing, and returning empty containers.</p>\n<p>Trakking semi-automates the process of requesting empty containers, with 95% of requests being automatically approved within 15 seconds. Trucking companies using Trakking can see real-time data on empty container inventories at various off-docks and ports, enabling them to choose the best location for pick-up and return, thus reducing unnecessary trips and optimizing operations.</p>\n<p>The real-time data on Trakking drastically reduces dead runs for truckers &#8211; in fact, in the 10,000 transactions processed so far, there have only been 2 dead runs. Trakking&#8217;s single platform also makes it easy and efficient for trucking companies to manage all empty container returns and releases, as well as street turns.</p>\n<p>Trakking is a game-changer for supply chain efficiency, offering a centralized and automated solution that saves time, money, and resources for all parties involved in global trade. With Trakking, the frustration of inefficient container management is a thing of the past.</p>\n<h4><a href=\"https://letstalksupplychain.com/episode-314-breaking-through-business-borders-broaden-your-reach-with-lean-solutions-group\">Watch the podcast episode where we discuss maximizing container efficiency with Trakking. Click here!</a></h4>\n<p><iframe title=\"YouTube video player\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/hdYN4Ulzhs8\" width=\"640\" height=\"498\" frameborder=\"0\" allowfullscreen=\"allowfullscreen\"></iframe></p>\n<h2>About the Author</h2>\n<p style=\"text-align: left;\"><img fetchpriority=\"high\" decoding=\"async\" class=\"alignleft wp-image-17843 size-medium\" src=\"https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/06/048-patrick-lo-300x200.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"300\" height=\"200\" title=\"\" srcset=\"https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/06/048-patrick-lo-300x200.jpg 300w, https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/06/048-patrick-lo-1024x682.jpg 1024w, https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/06/048-patrick-lo-768x511.jpg 768w, https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/06/048-patrick-lo-1536x1022.jpg 1536w, https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/06/048-patrick-lo-2048x1363.jpg 2048w, https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/06/048-patrick-lo-600x399.jpg 600w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 300px) 100vw, 300px\" /></p>\n<div class=\"page\" title=\"Page 1\">\n<div class=\"layoutArea\">\n<div class=\"column\">\n<p>Patrick Lo is the President and Founder of Trakking. After obtaining an Honours Science degree from UBC and an MBA from the Richard Ivey School of Business, he started working in the logistics industry in the early 1990s. In 2018 Patrick founded Trakking, a software company that provides a smarter way to do empty container logistics in Canada. In 2021, Trakking was one of the first software companies to be awarded a $1.3 million grant from the Canadian federal government to further develop its platform to increase efficiencies in Canada’s supply chain. Since launching its platform last year, hundreds of trucking companies are using Trakking to access valuable empty container data, receive automated approvals of street turns and empty container releases, and make better decisions.</p>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n",

  {
    "uuid": "560a4c8a-8647-49de-bcd2-7aded39856a8",
    "post_id": 17767,
    "type": "blogs",
    "title": "How to Choose the Right Last-Mile Delivery Technology for Your Business",
    "slug": "how-to-choose-the-right-last-mile-delivery-technology-for-your-business",
    "date": "2023-06-15T18:11:37",
    "summary": null,
    "main_points": null,
    "recent_news": null,
    "related_articles": [],
    "web_content": "<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Last-mile delivery is complex. It’s a challenge that shippers and carriers worldwide are battling every day. Will my deliveries reach my customers on time? How do I know which route is the shortest and the fastest for my deliveries? How do I manage my fleet? How can I keep track of all my deliveries? </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The solution to all these queries and various other challenges associated with last-mile delivery is quite straightforward: make a strategic investment in a robust last-mile delivery technology solution. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">However, the million-dollar question is how do you take the next step? How do you buy a last-mile delivery technology that best fits your needs and requirements? It&#8217;s a pressing concern that weighs heavily on the minds of many industry leaders.</span></p>\n<h2><b>Buy vs Build</b></h2>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Before companies dive into implementing last-mile delivery technology for their business, they must carefully consider whether building their own or purchasing existing technology makes the most sense. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Shippers and carriers can choose to build a last-mile delivery technology if they have the financial resources and technical expertise to do so. Creating something from the ground up also needs time. Additionally, the process does not end once the in-house last-mile delivery technology is implemented. The IT teams responsible for these systems must ensure that they are regularly updated and maintained. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">For many companies, however, building software is not part of their core competencies, and existing solutions in the market make more financial and operational sense. Purchasing last-mile technology nearly always guarantees faster deployment times and reduced capital expenditure. Further, companies that specialize in last-mile technology development are more likely to customize solutions and adapt to changing technologies more quickly</span></p>\n<h2><b>Key Considerations for Choosing the Right Last-Mile Delivery Technology</b></h2>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Once shippers and carriers decide that they want to invest in buying a last-mile delivery technology, they must consider the following factors before making their selection:</span></p>\n<p><b>Scalability:</b><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> The last-mile delivery technology must be flexible enough to adjust to the business needs of the shippers and carriers. An adaptive last-mile delivery technology will ensure that companies can not only smoothly handle their current volume of deliveries but also easily scale up when there’s an increase in delivery volumes. </span></p>\n<p><b>Integration capabilities:</b><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> Can your last-mile delivery technology effortlessly sync up with your existing systems? Consider how well the last-mile delivery technology can integrate with your existing systems, such as order management, inventory management, and customer relationship management (CRM) platforms. Seamless integration can streamline operations and is the key to improved efficiency.</span></p>\n<p><b>Customization options:</b><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> Evaluate whether the technology can be configured according to your business goals and specific requirements. For example, as a shipper, you may need a white-label last-mile delivery service. Or maybe you need tech that is specifically built for efficient big &amp; bulky last-mile deliveries.</span></p>\n<p><b>Real-time tracking and visibility:</b><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> Tracking and visibility are one of the most important components of any last-mile delivery technology. Look for features like the ability to monitor driver locations, estimated arrival times, and notifications for customers. Such features enhance transparency and improve customer satisfaction. They help shippers and carriers in identifying gaps in deliveries and taking proactive measures to fill them. </span></p>\n<p><b>Route optimization and planning:</b><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> Check if the technology offers advanced algorithms for route optimization and planning. Efficient routing can help reduce delivery time, and fuel costs, and improve overall productivity.</span></p>\n<p><b>Driver management tools:</b><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> Consider whether the technology provides tools for managing and optimizing driver assignments, scheduling, and performance tracking. These features can help streamline driver operations and improve productivity.</span></p>\n<p><b>Analytics and reporting:</b><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> Last-mile delivery technology must act as a repository of all the data involved in making deliveries. It should have in-built analytics and reporting capabilities. It should provide insights into delivery performance, metrics, and trends. This data can help identify areas for improvement and inform strategic decision-making.</span></p>\n<p><b>Customer support and training:</b><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> Customer support is critical when buying a last-mile delivery technology. The technology providers must provide adequate support to set up the system and once this has been done, they must resolve any technical issues that happen. Shippers and carriers should make sure their staff receives thorough training to handle future challenges effectively.</span></p>\n<p><b>Cost and ROI:</b><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> When selecting a last-mile delivery technology, companies must carefully assess the associated costs. These expenses typically are upfront payments, subscription fees, and potentially renewal charges as well. Shippers and carriers must calculate the potential return on investment (ROI) of the technology. </span></p>\n<p><b>Future-proofing:</b><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> Technologies get outdated and quickly become obsolete. When investing in any last-mile delivery technology assess the technology provider&#8217;s commitment towards regular updates and innovation. An up-to-date last-mile delivery technology is the first step towards greater efficiency, seamless operations, and enhanced consumer experience.</span></p>\n<h2><b>In Conclusion</b></h2>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The last-mile delivery market is brimming with technology that can help improve delivery operations. Shippers and carriers need to comprehensively evaluate the most suitable last-mile delivery technology to enhance their operations and meet their customers&#8217; expectations.</span></p>\n<h3>Resources:</h3>\n<p><a href=\"https://fareye.com/buyers-guide?utm_content=229002418\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Buyer&#8217;s Guide: How to Buy Last-mile Delivery Technology</span></a></p>\n<p><a href=\"https://fareye.com/resources/blogs/what-is-shipping-process\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The Ultimate Guide on Shipping Process</span></a></p>\n<p><a href=\"https://fareye.com/resources/reports-guides/eye-on-last-mile-logistics\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Report: Eye on last-mile for logistics</span></a></p>\n<h4><a href=\"https://letstalksupplychain.com/episode-314-breaking-through-business-borders-broaden-your-reach-with-lean-solutions-group\">Watch the podcast episode where we discuss the Last Minute Last Mile with FarEye.     "title": "10 Steps Trade Show &#038; Event Managers Can Take to Save Money and Improve the Logistics of Their Next Event",
    "slug": "10-steps-trade-show-event-managers-can-take-to-save-money-and-improve-the-logistics-of-their-next-event",
    "date": "2023-06-08T17:19:16",
    "summary": null,
    "main_points": null,
    "recent_news": null,
    "related_articles": [],
    "web_content": "<h1>10 Steps Trade Show &amp; Event Managers Can Take to Save Money and Improve the Logistics of Their Next Event</h1>\n<p>&nbsp;</p>\n<p>The logistics of trade show assets can make or break an event. A small error in the planning or execution of a trade show shipment can increase the cost of exhibiting or result in exhibit materials missing from the show- jeopardizing a company’s investment. For event planners looking to improve their processes and reduce the cost of attending large events this year, logistics is an important variable to review. Awareness, preparation, and careful management of shipment timing can help save money and protect a company’s trade show investment.</p>\n<h3>The team at EFW Tradeshow has compiled a list of 10 action items for event managers to improve the logistics of their next event.</h3>\n<p>&nbsp;</p>\n<p>1. Review your company’s entire show schedule and proactively plan. The logistics required to attend back-to-back shows can be cost-prohibitive if not considered well in advance. A plan that includes shipment planning, short-term storage solutions, temporary warehousing, and caravans can help save money.</p>\n<p>2. Be aware of the deadlines listed in the event manual. Pay attention to the deadlines listed in the event manual, including timelines for shipping to the advance warehouse or show site, targeted move-in/out, and forced dates and times. Surcharges for missed deadlines can increase exhibitor fees and lead to timeline issues with delivery and booth installation.</p>\n<p>3. Understand how drayage fees are calculated. Drayage, or material handling, is the roundtrip charge exhibitors pay to transport freight from the back of the carrier’s truck to the event space, and the return trip after the show is complete. Drayage can be charged as a flat fee, on a price per pound, or per hundred pounds basis. It is important to understand how your show calculates drayage and to follow the guidelines. This cost can account for a significant percentage of an exhibitor’s show budget.</p>\n<p>4. Package freight carefully and appropriately. Use crates, pallets, bubble wrap and foam padding to protect your exhibit assets during transit. Additionally- make sure your carrier knows they are loading the truck for a trade show delivery. Special handling fees for shipments that require additional time, labor, and equipment to unload, as defined in the show kit, will increase the cost of drayage.</p>\n<p>5. Label each shipment piece and remove old labels. Information such as company name, booth number, and number of packages on each piece increases the chance that your shipment will arrive on time. Without this information, pieces could get lost.</p>\n<p>6. Weigh and dimensionalize your freight before shipping to reduce billing errors. The weight listed on your Bill of Lading (BOL) should be completed accurately. This is often used by the event to determine drayage costs or provide you support if the drayage costs are inaccurate.</p>\n<p>7. Ask your carrier about wait time. Venue marshaling yards and wait times can cost you money. Carriers can wait in a marshaling yard for hours before being called to the dock for delivery or pick up. Check with your carrier to see how they are calculating wait time costs to ensure you don’t get hit with surprise charges.</p>\n<p>8. Complete and submit your material handling agreement (MHA) at the end of the show to reduce forced freight charges. The MHA informs the General Service Contractor (GSC) that your materials are ready for transit, and without it, the GSC will not release the freight to your carrier and may “force” your shipment by sending your materials back to the advance warehouse or the next destination using their carrier of choice. Submit this document on time and send a picture to your carrier.</p>\n<p>9. Review your insurance policy and understand your existing coverage. Too often, exhibitors assume that their assets are covered under the company’s corporate policy. However, many policies limit protections or don’t protect all property in transit or when it is temporarily away from the business location. Consider additional coverage options to protect yourself from unanticipated expenses.</p>\n<p>10. Consider a transportation partner that specializes in trade show shipping. Carriers with experience in handling exhibit materials safely and delivering them to event venues have the specialized equipment and infrastructure in place to get your materials there on time and in one piece. Add-ons like proactive planning, short-term storage, and on-site support can save time and money. The EFW Tradeshow team is devoted exclusively to special event transportation and logistics support. For more than 20 years, we have been helping companies improve efficiencies and reduce transportation costs. Contact our team to see if we can help support the logistics of your next event shipment.</p>\n<p>&nbsp;</p>\n<h4><a href=\"https://letstalksupplychain.com/episode-289-achieve-control-capacity-care/\">Watch the podcast episode where we take a full dive with EFW. Click here!</a></h4>\n<p><iframe title=\"YouTube video player\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/1Vt2phFPeW0\" width=\"640\" height=\"498\" frameborder=\"0\" allowfullscreen=\"allowfullscreen\"></iframe></p>\n<h2>About the Author</h2>\n<p style=\"text-align: left;\"><img decoding=\"async\" class=\"alignleft wp-image-17514 size-medium\" src=\"https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/06/EFW-Screenshot-at-Jun-08-07-51-42-300x113.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"300\" height=\"113\" title=\"\" srcset=\"https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/06/EFW-Screenshot-at-Jun-08-07-51-42-300x113.png 300w, https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/06/EFW-Screenshot-at-Jun-08-07-51-42-768x289.png 768w, https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/06/EFW-Screenshot-at-Jun-08-07-51-42-600x225.png 600w, https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/06/EFW-Screenshot-at-Jun-08-07-51-42.png 849w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 300px) 100vw, 300px\" /></p>\n<div class=\"page\" title=\"Page 1\">\n<div class=\"layoutArea\">\n<div class=\"column\">\n<div class=\"page\" title=\"Page 1\">\n<div class=\"layoutArea\">\n<div class=\"column\">\n<p style=\"text-align: left;\">EFW is a leading domestic and international freight forwarder in the United States, providing customized logistics and warehousing solutions for clients around the world and across all industries via air, ground, and ocean freight.     "web_content": "<h1>Supply Chain Automation: Optimizing Cashflow in the Age of Uncertainty</h1>\n<p>&nbsp;</p>\n<p>It is said that in times of crisis, cash is king.</p>\n<p>Considering all the recent volatility today’s businesses are facing — supply chain slowdowns, rising interest rates, record-breaking inflation, inflamed geopolitical conflicts and lingering post-pandemic economic effects — it would appear that these words are undeniably pertinent as we close out Q2 2023.</p>\n<p>As a result, CFOs and COOs must reexamine their strategies and focus more of their attention on fortifying and proactively protecting the financial health of the organization.</p>\n<p>This moment is a unique opportunity to develop a plan of action — not only to minimize the common supply chain disruptions that all too often negatively affect working capital, but also build a more sustainable and resilient business model.</p>\n<h2><strong>Rethinking the supply chain</strong></h2>\n<p>Traditionally, turning inventory has occupied the top spot of most supply chain leaders’ to-do lists. However, due to the current crop of challenges, more of them are being asked to focus their attention on activities such as minimizing the amount of money tied up in inventory as well as the money held up in other parts of the organization.</p>\n<p>This has resulted in a shift of mindset — thinking of the supply chain not as a construct made up of disparate parts, but as something more holistic where every process has to work in concert to achieve a common goal.</p>\n<p>Within order management, for example, incorrect or incomplete orders slow down order entry cycle time and on-time deliveries which, in turn, impacts cash collection and cashflow. One weak link within processes such as <a href=\"https://www.esker.com/business-process-solutions/procure-pay/accounts-payable-automation-software/?utm_source=podcast1&amp;utm_medium=blog&amp;utm_campaign=LTSC\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\">accounts payable</a> (AP), <a href=\"https://www.esker.com/business-process-solutions/order-cash/customer-service-automation/order-management-automation-system/?utm_source=podcast1&amp;utm_medium=blog&amp;utm_campaign=LTSC\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\">order management</a> or <a href=\"https://www.esker.com/business-process-solutions/order-cash/accounts-receivable-management-software/?utm_source=podcast1&amp;utm_medium=blog&amp;utm_campaign=LTSC\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\">accounts receivable</a> (AR) can make all the difference.</p>\n<p>&nbsp;</p>\n<h2><strong>Automation: More than just another technology</strong></h2>\n<p>Document process automation has been around for decades. However, while it’s often regarded as a “down the road” aspiration for businesses looking to save time and money, it is quickly becoming a necessary solution for maintaining a successful and sustainable business model thanks to its much broader and more transformational impact.</p>\n<p>Global cloud platforms, such as the one Esker offers, help today’s businesses connect every part of the <a href=\"https://www.esker.com/business-process-solutions/procure-pay-process/?utm_source=podcast1&amp;utm_medium=blog&amp;utm_campaign=LTSC\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\">procure-to-pay (P2P)</a> and <a href=\"https://www.esker.com/business-process-solutions/order-cash-process/?utm_source=podcast1&amp;utm_medium=blog&amp;utm_campaign=LTSC\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\">order-to-cash (O2C)</a> process.</p>\n<p><img fetchpriority=\"high\" decoding=\"async\" class=\" wp-image-17474 aligncenter\" src=\"https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/06/Picture1-300x133.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"546\" height=\"242\" title=\"\" srcset=\"https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/06/Picture1-300x133.png 300w, https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/06/Picture1-768x340.png 768w, https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/06/Picture1-600x266.png 600w, https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/06/Picture1.png 977w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 546px) 100vw, 546px\" /></p>\n<p>By creating a collaborative environment of end-to-end efficiency, companies can shore up back-office activities such as paying bills, processing orders, and collecting cash, while transforming the way customers and suppliers interact within your organization.</p>\n<p>Automation solutions give supply chain leaders an added level of intelligence over the people, processes, and technology that constitute their day-to-day operations. Powered by AI technology, users have the ability to:</p>\n<ul>\n<li><strong>Coordinate </strong>the entire cash conversion cycle — from P2P to O2C — through a single interface</li>\n<li><strong>Perform </strong>critical P2P and O2C tasks in real-time thanks to end-to-end connectivity between all applications</li>\n<li><strong>Oversee </strong>live KPIs, individual or team performances, and the lifecycles of orders and invoices — with customizable dashboards and reporting</li>\n<li><strong>Automate </strong>all documents regardless of format, language, or transmission method</li>\n<li><strong>Manage </strong>local specificities via support of multi-languages, multi-currencies &amp; local compliance requirements</li>\n</ul>\n<p><strong><br />\nCashflow is the lifeblood of a business — ready to learn more about the benefits of automation? </strong>Learn more by listening to Esker’s appearance on the latest Let’s Talk Supply Chain podcast.</p>\n<p>&nbsp;</p>\n<h4><a href=\"https://letstalksupplychain.com/?p=16793&amp;preview=true\">Watch the podcast episode where we take a full dive with Esker.   {
    "uuid": "18d1b4be-e239-411c-a237-df3e8546db0a",
    "post_id": 17318,
    "type": "blogs",
    "title": "Logistics Complexity and the Strategic Moves Companies are Making to Reduce It",
    "slug": "logistics-complexity-and-the-strategic-moves-companies-are-making-to-reduce-it",
    "date": "2023-05-18T08:00:30",
    "summary": null,
    "main_points": null,
    "recent_news": null,
    "related_articles": [],
    "web_content": "<h1><strong>Logistics Complexity and the Strategic Moves Companies Are Making to Reduce It</strong></h1>\n<p>The last mile is typically the costliest and most complicated leg of a supply chain, accounting for, on average, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/last-mile-delivery-shipping-explained\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\">53% of overall shipping costs</a>. Last-mile delivery has become the center of attention for shippers and carriers in recent years as strong e-commerce growth has increased demand for home delivery.</p>\n<p>Stuck with legacy last-mile practices, logistics companies have struggled to meet consumer demand, which has compelled courier, express, and parcel (CEP) companies to rethink their last-mile delivery operations and how technology can play a role.</p>\n<p>Enterprises have started looking at technological innovations to simplify the last mile, investing in machine learning (ML) and artificial intelligence (AI) to automate processes such as scheduling and routing, improving supply chain visibility and reducing costs overall.</p>\n<p>&nbsp;</p>\n<h2><strong>Artificial Intelligence and Machine Learning’s Impact on Logistics Complexity</strong></h2>\n<p>Logistics companies are leaving no stone unturned in modernizing and streamlining their last-mile delivery operations. Recently, United Parcel Services (UPS) in collaboration with Google analyzed Radio Frequency Identification (RFID) data and used it to plan the most efficient routes for more than 25 million packages it delivers globally each day.</p>\n<p>Radio-frequency identification (RFID) technology helps logistics companies increase visibility into their last-mile operations. Visibility in the delivery process gives logistics companies more control over their last-mile operations.</p>\n<p>FedEx Dataworks, an organization embedded within the courier giant FedEx, harnesses the power of data science and ML to improve supply chain visibility. Dataworks uses AI to predict shipping times and accurate delivery dates.</p>\n<p>In the <a href=\"https://www.getfareye.com/insights/blog/the-last-mile-mandate-survey\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\">Last Mile Mandate survey</a> conducted by FarEye in 2022, U.S. consumers claim the ability to have delivery tracking as a top factor for creating a positive delivery experience. Logistics companies must invest in technologies that provide more visibility to not only their dispatch managers but to end consumers as well.</p>\n<p>Intelligent computer vision, an offshoot of AI, helps CEP companies automate repetitive tasks, handle massive shipments with ease and considerably reduce last-mile delivery complexities. Royal Mail recently opened Super Hub, with the latest scanning, sorting, and tracking technology. The hub is set to process close to 800,000 parcels per day.</p>\n<p>Postal companies like Swiss Post benefited from Autonomous Mobile Robots (AMRs), upping their parcel handling capacity to 40,000 parcels a day. Automation in the CEP industry is not restricted to warehouses and sorting centers. InPost, a parcel locker technology company, saw its profits rise by 67% thanks to investments made in deploying automated parcel machines (APMs).</p>\n<p>&nbsp;</p>\n<h2><strong>Rise of Drone Technology</strong></h2>\n<p>CEP companies are also embracing drone technology to help deliver packages quickly and efficiently across multiple locations. Skyports Drone Services, a UK-based division of an advanced air mobility company, has been selected by Royal Mail to manage aerial distribution routes linking Scotland&#8217;s Orkney islands. The drone service provider aims to enhance the efficiency and reliability of drone deliveries for Royal Mail, demonstrating the growing integration of unmanned aerial vehicles in the logistics industry.</p>\n<p>The CEP industry’s future is being reshaped by new-age technologies like AI, ML, robotics, big data analytics, cloud computing, and predictive analytics. Investments in tech are being made to make last-mile logistics simpler, more cost-efficient, and more customer-focused.</p>\n<h2><strong>Reducing Logistics Complexity and Delivering Superior Consumer Experiences</strong></h2>\n<p>&nbsp;</p>\n<p>According to <a href=\"https://www.mckinsey.com/industries/metals-and-mining/our-insights/succeeding-in-the-ai-supply-chain-revolution\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\">McKinsey</a>, successfully implementing AI-enabled supply-chain management has enabled early adopters to improve logistics costs by 15 percent, inventory levels by 35%, and service levels by 65%, compared with slower-moving competitors.</p>\n<p>The answer is clear: if companies want to simplify the most complicated aspects of delivery logistics, especially in the last mile, they must optimize their end-to-end omnichannel fulfillment with precision while minimizing last-mile costs.</p>\n<p>And to do so, they must pivot to modern technologies to reduce logistics complexity in their last mile operations with the end goal of delivering a superior consumer experience.</p>\n<h4><a href=\"https://letstalksupplychain.com/episode-314-breaking-through-business-borders-broaden-your-reach-with-lean-solutions-group\">Watch the podcast episode where we discuss the Last Minute Last Mile with FarEye. Click here!</a></h4>\n<p><iframe title=\"YouTube video player\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/xB22Hh6osRI\" width=\"640\" height=\"498\" frameborder=\"0\" allowfullscreen=\"allowfullscreen\"></iframe></p>\n<h2>About the Author</h2>\n<p style=\"text-align: left;\"><img fetchpriority=\"high\" decoding=\"async\" class=\"alignleft wp-image-16597 size-medium\" src=\"https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/04/Untitled-Vicki-Aasbjerg-Andersen-300x300.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"300\" height=\"300\" title=\"\" srcset=\"https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/04/Untitled-Vicki-Aasbjerg-Andersen-300x300.png 300w, https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/04/Untitled-Vicki-Aasbjerg-Andersen-1024x1024.png 1024w, https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/04/Untitled-Vicki-Aasbjerg-Andersen-150x150.png 150w, https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/04/Untitled-Vicki-Aasbjerg-Andersen-768x768.png 768w, https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/04/Untitled-Vicki-Aasbjerg-Andersen-600x600.png 600w, https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/04/Untitled-Vicki-Aasbjerg-Andersen-100x100.png 100w, https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/04/Untitled-Vicki-Aasbjerg-Andersen.png 1439w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 300px) 100vw, 300px\" /></p>\n<div class=\"page\" title=\"Page 1\">\n<div class=\"layoutArea\">\n<div class=\"column\">\n<p>Jorge Lopera has over 15 years of global logistics experience in senior roles encompassing customer growth, product management, and strategy.   {
    "uuid": "2aaa4d67-e9fc-419a-a31f-94844f5310d9",
    "post_id": 16806,
    "type": "blogs",
    "title": "Fulfillment Plus Value Added Services: A Magic Formula",
    "slug": "fulfillment-plus-value-added-services-a-magic-formula",
    "date": "2023-05-04T09:00:36",
    "summary": null,
    "main_points": null,
    "recent_news": null,
    "related_articles": [],
    "web_content": "<h1>Fulfillment Plus Value Added Services: A Magic Formula</h1>\n<p>&nbsp;</p>\n<p style=\"text-align: left;\">Renewal Logistics handles warehousing and distribution as most 3PLs do, but where we are very different is that <strong>we are the ONLY 3PL that I know of in the US that also does Value Added Services projects at scale. And when I say Only, I mean Only.</strong> I was at an <a href=\"https://iwla.com/\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\">International Warehousing and Logistics Association</a> function a few weeks ago, and we were the ONLY company out of about 150 in the room that did Value Added Services as a primary function of our business. As it turns out the combination of fulfillment and value-added services in a single-sourced provider is a magic formula for success.</p>\n<h2 style=\"text-align: left;\">What Are Value-Added Services?</h2>\n<p>Any Projects Or Programs That Are Needed To Prepare A Product To Ship.</p>\n<p>This Includes:</p>\n<ul>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.renewallogistics.com/amazon-fba-prep-services/\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\">Amazon FBA Prep</a></li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.renewallogistics.com/ecommerce-and-retail-fulfillment/\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\">Wholesale Distribution prep</a></li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.renewallogistics.com/apparel-services/\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\">Kitting</a></li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.renewallogistics.com/services/\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\">Product Auditing for E-commerce Fulfillment</a></li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.renewallogistics.com/subscription-box-fulfillment/\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\">Subscription box assembly</a></li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.renewallogistics.com/logistic-services/\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\">End cap display assembly</a></li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.renewallogistics.com/mold-remediation-services/\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\">Cleaning or remediation services</a></li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.renewallogistics.com/returns-and-circularity-services/\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\">Returns</a></li>\n</ul>\n<h2>Why Are Value-Added Services Important To Brands Choosing A 3PL?</h2>\n<p>&nbsp;</p>\n<h3>Client Story</h3>\n<p>I had a client recently who came to us and said that they had a product that was at a particular 3PL warehouse that had a promo insert that was in violation of Amazon’s policies, so they needed to remove these promo inserts from all of their products that were intended for Amazon FBA.</p>\n<p>They could never get the warehouse where these goods were stored, to get them to agree to handle this project, and they ultimately never were able to get the project complete at the warehouse. After months of trying, they ended up having to open a temporary space, have all the product shipped to them, they had to manually remove the inserts, and then had to ship the product back to the warehouse.</p>\n<p>What a hassle and what an expense!! Not only the shipping and transfer expense of moving the product, but the lost time of the managers who had to stop working on things to grow the business, who had to divert their time to managing this project, and then also think about the lost sales.</p>\n<p>On the flip side, what we offer to companies is the ability to harness the potential of each and every product.</p>\n<p>The most successful brands in the world are watching their inventory and making adjustments in a very fluid way. And they capture a lot of extra sales because they have this flexibility.</p>\n<h2>How, You Ask?</h2>\n<p><strong>As an Example:</strong> One client had 800,000 units of single-packed women’s undergarments that didn’t sell through to Walmart. We accepted the return, bundled the returned units into 5 packs, created PDQs which we loaded with these 5 packs, and then our client resold ALL of that product to Walmart again.  And then the product did sell through.</p>\n<p>Another client had a 1.7MM unit order canceled by one major big box retailer. We accepted that return and rebranded all of those items so that the product could be sold to another large retailer within a few weeks, allowing this client to still capitalize on the seasonality of the product.</p>\n<p><strong>There are tons of examples like this. For instance, today at our facility we are doing </strong><strong>the following:</strong></p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.renewallogistics.com/logistic-services/\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"><strong>Wholesale Prep:</strong></a> Today we’re taking 30,000 units of undergarments that came in from the factory in universal packaging, and customizing it for our clients’ wholesale customers’ vendor requirements.</p>\n<p>For instance, some companies like bag tags on the bottom right of a polybag, some like bag tags in the middle, and some like bag tags on the bottom left corner. Some want sports bras folded in half in the polybag, some want them unfolded in polybags. Today, we are prepping products for Urban Outfitters, Macy&#8217;s, Kohls.com, Bealls, and many many more. Every Retailer has a different set of requirements and on a given day we may be prepping product scheduled to go to 40-50 different retailers. We manage vendor guides for about 145 retailer clients.</p>\n<p>This means, our clients can be dynamic, selling as many products as they want to any of these 145 retailers, and within a few days have that product prepped and shipped.</p>\n<p><strong><a href=\"https://www.renewallogistics.com/amazon-fba-prep-services/\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\">Amazon FBA Prep</a>:</strong> We are the largest FBA prep facility in the country that we know of, and we do some days tens of thousands of units of FBA prep. Getting product packed in the right quantities, and with the right labels, creating shipping plans, etc for these goods to go to an Amazon Distribution Center. Amazon has exacting standards on how products are to arrive, and if items do not conform, there are high fees for fixing those issues. Today we’re prepping about 15,000 units for an athleisure brand to be sent to Amazon FBA.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.renewallogistics.com/apparel-services/\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"><strong>Kitting:</strong></a> We have a client right now that is asking us to print user manuals for one of their mechanical desks, and create kits consisting of those user manuals, the desk, and a riser. Our system is able to account for what quantities of stock are consumed by the kits so that the inventory stays clean in our WMS, and our employees physically create these kits, including labeling the bundle with a new SKU or UPC code.</p>\n<p><strong><a href=\"https://www.renewallogistics.com/e-commerce-and-retail-fulfillment/\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\">E-commerce Fulfillment Prep – Auditing:</a></strong> Today we are handling all of the audits for a client’s product that ultimately goes to Kohls.com for fulfillment. Kohls has very strict policies and chargebacks. The major challenge is that the chargebacks are based on a percentage of goods audited. But, if a problem is located, Kohls will increase the percentage of goods that must be audited from 2% to 5% to 10%. For each level of audit, the fees for nonconforming units go up. I saw a recent chargeback for $800 for 1 case with a wrinkled case label. By taking over this auditing process for this client, they’ve been able to go from a “D” to a “B” level vendor, in less than 6 months. In another 6 months, they’ll be an “A” level vendor!</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.renewallogistics.com/subscription-box-fulfillment/\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"><strong>Subscription Box Assembly:</strong></a> We have a client that sells baby clothes that we’re creating gift boxes that include onesie sets, as well as bathing products, and a washcloth and towel. They are all put into a box in a certain order so that there is a beautiful unboxing experience.</p>\n<p>These are going out as a subscription box, but this client is also able to offer this gift as a stand-alone product through their holiday sales channels.</p>\n<p>We also perform gift wrapping for this client, so they’re able to increase their average revenue per order – without having to do this in-house, which would slow down their own facility and distract their own workforce.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.renewallogistics.com/logistic-services/\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"><strong>End Cap Display Assembly:</strong></a> We are finalizing the shipments for 3,800 end cap displays that are going to Walmart to be on display through the holiday season. They came to us as flat corrugated pieces that we had to shape into an end cap display PDQ, and then fill with product, then create the outer shipper case and palletize. There were 50 different products<br />\non each display, in quantities of 5-20 units per SKU, to total around 450 different units on each display. At the end of the project, the <strong>3,800 displays were filled with over 1,710,000 </strong><strong>units of product.</strong> We do these with 100% accuracy. We’ve never failed an audit.</p>\n<p>This client was able to offer the creation of this end cap display program to Walmart to differentiate their products from their competition. It got their foot in the door for a much larger sales program than they were originally considered for.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.renewallogistics.com/mold-remediation-services/\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"><strong>Cleaning and Remediation Services:</strong></a> We’re doing a project right now of belts that came over from the factory for an accessories company, that had a musty smell and had some mildew. Apparently, the container had a moisture issue- which isn’t surprising since it sat on the water for an extra 90 days due to the port delays. We’re decontaminating this product so<br />\nthat it can be sold as first quality. We lab test goods to be sure that there is no contamination remaining. We’re cleaning about 30,000 belts in our facility this week.</p>\n<p>We also from time to time work with brands who have product that does not conform to the compliance guidelines for their retailers, and we will remediate nonconforming product so that it can be properly sold.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.renewallogistics.com/returns-and-circularity-services/\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"><strong>Returns:</strong></a> We manage the returns programs for some of the largest apparel retailers in the world. Today we’re doing a 45,000 unit return project of goods that were sold to Nike that didn’t sell through. We’re crediting and repackaging the goods so that they can be sold as new to the next retailer.</p>\n<p>On top of this, we’re handling our normal distribution and fulfillment for our B2B and B2C e-commerce clients. And trust me when I tell you, picking and packing is the easy part!</p>\n<p>Our clients love about our specific ability to handle Value Added Services at Scale, which is the flexibility it provides our clients in their wholesale sales programs.</p>\n<h2>Looking For More?</h2>\n<p>If you ever want to chat with our existing clients, many of them we have NDAs with, so I<br />\ncan’t share their names on the website or in our newsletter, but I assure you, you’ve purchased product from them,  and if you want to verify our consistency, accuracy, and ability to handle complexity with ease, they’ll be happy to talk to you.</p>\n<p>&nbsp;</p>\n<h4><a href=\"https://letstalksupplychain.com/episode-332-make-fulfilment-easy-and-sustainable-with-renewal-logistics/\">Watch the podcast episode where we take a full dive with Renewal Logistics. Click here!</a></h4>\n<p><iframe title=\"YouTube video player\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/T3TdBiTQlZE\" width=\"640\" height=\"498\" frameborder=\"0\" allowfullscreen=\"allowfullscreen\"></iframe></p>\n<h2>About the Author</h2>\n<p style=\"text-align: left;\"><img fetchpriority=\"high\" decoding=\"async\" class=\"alignleft wp-image-16427 size-medium\" src=\"https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/04/renewal-logistics-courtney-folk-300x201.png\" alt=\"Courtney Folk shares her thoughts on Fulfillment, Returns and Value Added Services are Magic when Combined \" width=\"300\" height=\"201\" title=\"\" srcset=\"https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/04/renewal-logistics-courtney-folk-300x201.png 300w, https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/04/renewal-logistics-courtney-folk.png 450w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 300px) 100vw, 300px\" /></p>\n<div class=\"page\" title=\"Page 1\">\n<div class=\"layoutArea\">\n<div class=\"column\">\n<div class=\"page\" title=\"Page 1\">\n<div class=\"layoutArea\">\n<div class=\"column\">\n<p>As CEO and co-founder of Renewal Logistics, my mission is to help companies of all sizes grow and thrive. I especially find fulfillment in helping other female-led businesses reach their full potential. Even during unpredictable times, I strive to help our clients build sustainable processes and serve their customers a high-quality experience</p>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n",
