  {
    "uuid": "50957798-fb36-4b67-887f-7480b7832d74",
    "post_id": 12744,
    "type": "blogs",
    "title": "To Visibility and Beyond: Overcoming 3PL/LSP Challenges in 2022",
    "slug": "to-visibility-and-beyond-overcoming-3pl-lsp-challenges-in-2022",
    "date": "2022-04-01T00:28:40",
    "summary": null,
    "main_points": null,
    "recent_news": null,
    "related_articles": [],
    "web_content": "<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The last few years haven’t been without their challenges. Supply chain disruptions catapulted our industry to the tip of the public’s tongue. And the ride isn’t quite over yet. As we’re rearing our heads above water, 2022 presents a whole new set of challenges for 3PLs and LSPs.</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">But luckily, Fourkites’ already started to find solutions to these predicted struggles. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Today we’re bringing you an exclusive perspective from Raj Patel, VP of Industry Strategy, 3PLs.</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">By the end of this, you’ll understand the three pressing challenges for third-party logistic providers (3PLs) or logistic service providers (LSPs) and Raj’s key insights on how to overcome them.</span></p>\n<h3><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Current Supply Chain Trends for 3PLs and LSPs Are Creating New Challenges</span></h3>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">It’s hard to nail down all of the obstacles facing the industry. But Patel offers 3PLs and LSPs three key areas to pay attention to.</span></p>\n<ul>\n<li style=\"font-weight: 400;\" aria-level=\"1\"><b>Labor. </b><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Supply chainers will be the first to tell you that labor’s been an issue. So, it’s important to pay attention to how you’re using your current labor, how you recruit, and how you retain. It’s about balancing your labor compared to robotics and having visibility to where your labor is.</span></li>\n<li style=\"font-weight: 400;\" aria-level=\"1\"><b>Cost. </b><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">We’ve heard about inflation &#8211; but who actually pays for the rising costs? Have a plan in place to understand where this increase flows.</span></li>\n<li style=\"font-weight: 400;\" aria-level=\"1\"><b>Innovation. </b><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The future is here and it’s about time to think about how robotics (autonomous vehicles, picking, etc.) fits into your business, how your supply chain affects environmental, social, and governance (ESG) goals, distribution center locations and implementable technology.</span></li>\n</ul>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Blowing in with the trends listed above are the new services having to be offered by 3PLs and LSPs. They’re stepping out of their comfort zones, and we’re here for it. </span></p>\n<h3><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Value-Added Services are the New Black</span></h3>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Industry changes mean a new dynamic of operations. In order to keep up with the waves of change, logistic providers are having to roll up their sleeves and offer new services. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Being innovative with what you provide to clients is going to add a significant amount of value to your business and customers. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Historically done in field-stocking locations, logistic providers can determine where warehouses are needed to reach 90% of the U.S. population. . 3PLs are making more logical, logistical choices. But they still need more, smaller microfufillmment centers in order to reach 90% within the one-day delivery consumers expect. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">So how can they get there? With the help of artificial intelligence/machine learning. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">And while LSPs have usually stayed in their own lane with basic monthly forecasts, Patel tells us they’re now pulling up a seat to the table with their client’s marketing, sales, and operations teams. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Why? </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">For visibility in planning in order to identify which products are super important. Are there campaigns that will affect planning? 3PLs are starting to get their hands dirty in this essential execution process. The result is a smoother start-to-finish, higher sales, and increased customer satisfaction. </span></p>\n<h3><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Mitigating Risk in a New, Risky World</span></h3>\n<p><i><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">“The new normal.” “Unprecedented times.”</span></i><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> Just a few of the buzzwords our team at Let&#8217;s Talk Supply Chain™ hears all the time. Along with </span><i><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">“agility”</span></i><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> and </span><i><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">“resilience”</span></i><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">But Patel stresses to us that this agility and resilience always comes with a price. For example, in order to be agile and resilient, you might have to be tripled-sourced which will come at a cost to your overall supply chain.</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">That safety-stock and extra inventory that was once frowned upon is now expected. A question probed by Patel, “What if the war in Europe doesn’t end? What if the Suez Canal happens again?” It’s these sort of world events that we’re not used to that we now, well, have to get used to.</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">In order to mitigate risk, Patel also encourages you to know your suppliers and vendors—and who they’re getting their materials from. In essence, don’t put all of your eggs into one basket.</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Micro-fulfillment centers (MFCs) and other strategies can deliver you to agility and resilience, but beware of that fine balance between cost and risk. </span></p>\n<h3><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Visibility is Good, But Actionable Visibility is Better</span></h3>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Gaining visibility to your supply chain is one thing. And while the ability to see where your container is at sea or on the road is possible, Patel argues that having actionable visibility is a whole other storm. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Because really, what is it exactly that we might do with that visibility once we get it? </span><a href=\"https://www.fourkites.com/platform/real-time-visibility/\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Fourkites’ visibility platform</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> allows companies to identify implementable strategies and make confident, prosperous decisions through tons of predictive analytics and machine learning. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">It’s something I can get behind—no more guessing, no more surprises. We’ll always find ways to pivot, supply chainers! So let’s go to visibility and beyond!</span></p>\n",

    "uuid": "52f92c39-9266-4c28-bef8-6a0eb650820b",
    "post_id": 12725,
    "type": "blogs",
    "title": "Mastering Crisis: Lessons from Covid-19",
    "slug": "mastering-crisis-lessons-from-covid-19",
    "date": "2022-03-29T04:00:31",
    "summary": null,
    "main_points": null,
    "recent_news": null,
    "related_articles": [],
    "web_content": "<p>The Covid-19 pandemic has caused unprecedented interruptions and challenges in almost every sector of business, including logistics and the supply chain. In 2020 when Covid first emerged as a global crisis and businesses began to temporarily shut down or reduce their operations, the global economy was temporarily turned off. As more information became available and as some mitigation strategies were put in place, the economy quickly rebounded, creating an environment where shipping demand outpaced market capacity. With many consumers spending more time at home and having access to more disposable income than in recent history, demand for goods raised retail volumes, specifically with-in the e-commerce space that are now years ahead of schedule with a supply chain that has struggled to keep up. From back-logs at ports, to driver shortages, to reduced equipment availability and an overall lack of predictability and precision, logistics companies along with shippers had to respond quickly in order to best meet their business needs in this new environment.</p>\n<p><strong>Here are some Do’s and Don’ts that can help guide businesses through any crisis:</strong></p>\n<h4>Do’s</h4>\n<ul>\n<li>If you have not done so already &#8211; establish clear business needs and goals. This may seem obvious but to navigate any type of crisis, one should truly understand what the needs and goals of the business are and where the business is headed. Every major business decision should be aligned with achieving those goals. If you already have a plan but have had to “look under the hood”, it would be a good time to do an overall review of the business and reassess the goals of your organization.</li>\n<li>Be ready and willing to pivot when a scenario is not going as expected. Use existing resources in new ways to adapt to quickly changing situations. “This is how we always do things” and like language needs to be eliminated from your vocabulary. Do take the situation that your business is facing as an opportunity to be your own consultant with-in your business and to be a stronger leader and company as a result of it.</li>\n<li>Engage your partnerships and work together. Have open and candid conversations with vendors, clients, customers and staff about the challenges that have come up. With clear communication, these relationships can be strengthened and keep everyone working with synergy towards a common goal. The strongest partnerships are ones where expectations from all parties are understood and in alignment with the business goals.</li>\n</ul>\n<h4>Don’ts</h4>\n<ul>\n<li>Don’t overreact and throw away what is working. Trust what your company has done to become successful and continue to invest in the people and processes that support this success. “Stay calm and trust the process.”</li>\n<li>Although you should not overreact, don’t expect to see different results if nothing changes. In times of adversity and uncertainty, doing nothing and “hoping” things will get better is not always the best strategy.</li>\n<li>Don’t be the victim. It can be too easy to want to blame external factors that you may have limited to zero control over, such as the economy and the overall environment that may be impacting your business in a negative way. Focus on what you can control and do not make excuses.</li>\n</ul>\n<p>Adapting to adversity in uncertain times requires a deft willingness to meet the moment. With agility, clear communication and the willingness to think and act differently, companies can position themselves to not Only survive a crisis, but to be better because of it.</p>\n<h2>About the Author</h2>\n<p><img fetchpriority=\"high\" decoding=\"async\" class=\"wp-image-12729 size-medium alignleft\" src=\"https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/083-Ashley-Caloia-300x200.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"300\" height=\"200\" title=\"\" srcset=\"https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/083-Ashley-Caloia-300x200.jpg 300w, https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/083-Ashley-Caloia-1024x683.jpg 1024w, https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/083-Ashley-Caloia-768x512.jpg 768w, https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/083-Ashley-Caloia-1536x1024.jpg 1536w, https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/083-Ashley-Caloia-2048x1365.jpg 2048w, https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/083-Ashley-Caloia-600x400.jpg 600w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 300px) 100vw, 300px\" /></p>\n<div class=\"freebirdFormviewerViewNumberedItemContainer\" role=\"listitem\">\n<div class=\"freebirdFormviewerViewItemsItemItem freebirdFormviewerViewItemsTextTextItem\" data-required=\"true\" data-item-id=\"254210850\">\n<div class=\"freebirdFormviewerViewItemsTextTextItemContainer\">\n<div class=\"freebirdFormviewerViewItemsTextLongText freebirdFormviewerViewItemsTextDisabledText freebirdThemedInput\">Kristy Knichel, a lifelong Pittsburgh native, is a second-generation logistics executive. She is CEO of <a href=\"http://www.knichellogistics.com\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\">Knichel Logistics, Inc.</a> and presently holds the Intermodal Logistics Conference Chair on the TIA Board of Directors.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<div class=\"freebirdFormviewerViewNumberedItemContainer\" role=\"listitem\">\n<div class=\"freebirdFormviewerViewItemsItemItem\" data-required=\"true\" data-input=\"L9xHkb\" data-item-id=\"1609135432\">\n<div class=\"freebirdFormviewerViewItemsItemItemHeader\">\n<div class=\"freebirdFormviewerViewItemsItemItemTitleDescContainer\">\n<div class=\"freebirdFormviewerViewItemsItemItemTitleContainer\"></div>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n",

    "uuid": "bfca6026-3e16-4809-82f5-5794411e6486",
    "post_id": 12706,
    "type": "blogs",
    "title": "Why Data, Focus and Follow-Through Are Shaping the Future of Supply Chain",
    "slug": "why-data-focus-and-follow-through-are-shaping-the-future-of-supply-chain",
    "date": "2022-03-26T04:00:22",
    "summary": null,
    "main_points": null,
    "recent_news": null,
    "related_articles": [],
    "web_content": "<p>The proverb that the journey of a thousand miles begins with a single step might seem like an amusing paradox for supply chain professionals. On the one hand, the road to digital maturity is daunting, and many companies are only just setting out on the path to end-to-end visibility and intelligent risk management. Yet on the other hand, the journey itself might not be well-defined, let alone the destination.</p>\n<p>Overhaul sponsored the recent <a href=\"https://gdssummits.com/event/supply-chain-insight-summit-na-feb-22/\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\">GDS North America Supply Chain Digital Summit</a>, helping to light a path through the big questions supply chain leaders – who represent some of the world’s largest technology, pharmaceutical, retail and manufacturing companies – continue to confront along their journeys. Read on to learn the three key themes that emerged and insights for each from <a href=\"https://www.linkedin.com/in/frankiemossman/\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\">Frankie Mossman</a>, Overhaul’s Chief Customer Officer.</p>\n<p><strong>Smart data make smart supply chains</strong></p>\n<p>Supply chain leaders recognize that now is the time to make big investments and bold decisions. <a href=\"https://www.gartner.com/en/newsroom/2021-02-10-gartner-survey-finds-87-of-supply-chain-professionals-plan-to-invest-in-resilience-within-the-next-2-years\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\">A 2021 Gartner survey</a> found that nearly 90 percent planned to invest in supply chain resilience, and 80 percent said that new technology would be needed over the next three years. But technology is only one component of smart supply chains.</p>\n<p>“Data is everywhere, and it can be overwhelming,” says Frankie. “But we need to make it manageable and actionable so that we can make better decisions and orchestrate across the entire supply-chain ecosystem.” Smart supply chains are defined by the problems they solve, not the technology or software they use. “A smart supply chain needs to know what’s happening,” Frankie explains, but it’s ultimately only as smart as the data we prioritize.</p>\n<p><strong>Agility versus resiliency</strong></p>\n<p>‘Agility’ and ‘resiliency’ are two words often used interchangeably with respect to supply chain, notes Frankie, especially in recent news stories about disruptions and shortages. But they have a clear distinction. “Resiliency is making sure that you’re ready for the worst-case scenario, which means you do have to have more reserve stock and redundancies. Agility is taking advantage of an opportunity.”</p>\n<p>Over the past two years, virtually every industry has had to be more agile, especially in decision-making. “The pandemic forced us to make decisions much faster and get out of our comfort zones around how we use data and share information,” says Frankie. “But it also revealed where we weren’t resilient and didn’t have redundant sources of supply and inventory.”</p>\n<p>Similarly, companies shouldn’t interchange how they execute. “You need to have a strategy as to whether you want to be an agile or a resilient supply chain,” emphasizes Frankie. “Supply chains can be both, depending on the business models they support,” but this hybrid requires clear definition. Although it may seem counterintuitive, simultaneously pursuing agility and resilience could undermine how well a supply chain is equipped for the next seismic shift.</p>\n<p><strong>Transition versus transformation</strong></p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.mckinsey.com/business-functions/strategy-and-corporate-finance/our-insights/five-fifty-the-quickening\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\">According to McKinsey</a>, e-commerce in the US grew at a 10-year pace within the first quarter of 2020 and the onset of the pandemic. As consumers quickly transitioned to find alternatives to brick-and-mortar stores, they ignited a long-term transformation of how we source, manufacture and distribute goods across a full spectrum of industries.</p>\n<p>The tension between transition and transformation also fine-tunes supply chains. As Frankie puts it, “Transition is continuous improvement, where we take the building blocks that we have today and make them slightly better. Transformation is thinking completely differently.”</p>\n<p>She points to the 2021 blockage of the Suez Canal as another transformational flashpoint. Its aftermath spurred shippers to take short-term action like evaluating alternate routes, and underscored complex, long-term questions. Poor infrastructure, climate change and changing consumer behaviors all were contributing forces, and they will likely play significant roles in the event of a future similar incident. “We’re never going to have perfect data. But we can intelligently know the direction we need to go and how to take that next step.”</p>\n<p>A transformational mindset ultimately is what sets leading companies apart. “When you go on a transformational journey, you’re not going from zero to sixty,” says Frankie. “You don’t become a visible, smart supply chain tomorrow just because you plug in great software. It’s a journey that has iterations.”</p>\n<h5>About the Author</h5>\n<p>&nbsp;</p>\n<p><img decoding=\"async\" class=\"wp-image-12710 size-medium alignnone\" src=\"https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/OverhaulLogo_Original-2-Stephanie-Varty-300x49.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"300\" height=\"49\" title=\"\" srcset=\"https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/OverhaulLogo_Original-2-Stephanie-Varty-300x49.png 300w, https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/OverhaulLogo_Original-2-Stephanie-Varty-1024x167.png 1024w, https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/OverhaulLogo_Original-2-Stephanie-Varty-768x125.png 768w, https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/OverhaulLogo_Original-2-Stephanie-Varty-1536x250.png 1536w, https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/OverhaulLogo_Original-2-Stephanie-Varty-2048x333.png 2048w, https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/OverhaulLogo_Original-2-Stephanie-Varty-600x98.png 600w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 300px) 100vw, 300px\" />Founded in 2016 and headquartered in Austin, Texas, Overhaul is the industry’s first and only holistic, end-to-end solution that optimizes supply-chain visibility, integrity, and security for global enterprises. Its software-based approach offers high configurability and efficient time-to-value to supply-chain organizations without heavy tech. Additionally, Overhaul’s logistics-experts team partners with each client to create a fully customized and comprehensive solution for the entire supply chain. As such, Overhaul has quickly grown to be a trusted provider for Fortune 100 companies moving freight globally across industries, such as pharmaceutical and healthcare, technology, logistics, and food and beverage. Customers include Microsoft, Bristol Myers Squibb, Gordon Food Service, and many others.</p>\n",

    "uuid": "386f3a1e-84df-446c-9671-e86323efd0a3",
    "post_id": 12523,
    "type": "blogs",
    "title": "It’s Now 2022 – Are Consumers Growing Tired of Supply Chain Shortages and Rising Costs?",
    "slug": "its-now-2022-are-consumers-growing-tired-of-supply-chain-shortages-and-rising-costs",
    "date": "2022-03-12T04:00:45",
    "summary": null,
    "main_points": null,
    "recent_news": null,
    "related_articles": [],
    "web_content": "<p>Two years ago, when many of us first experienced the supply chain impacts of the pandemic, some situations were unprecedented – like empty store shelves, lack of availability of common household goods and only one means of shopping – e-commerce. Consumers adapted and anticipated a return to more typical conditions for purchasing CPG items. However, as new strains of the pandemic continue to emerge, along with inflation, those unprecedented events are becoming almost daily occurrences, along with rising prices for basic necessities.</p>\n<p>Clearly, the CPG sector faces many supply chain management challenges &#8211; everything from increasing costs for contract lanes due to a driver shortage, to containers sitting at ports for extended amounts of time. A solution &#8211; like shifting to air freight will solve the access to products, but significantly increase operating costs. Many CPG companies are increasing the price of goods to offset the cost of supply chain challenges. This begs the question – do CPGs face the risk of passing along such severe price hikes that consumers may not return once economic conditions stabilize?</p>\n<h4><strong>Diversification of suppliers and sourcing locations are no small tasks</strong></h4>\n<p>Some CPG companies have changed their supplier strategy from one with a few select suppliers to an increased number of vendors. Managing more vendors inherently requires more work on the part of the shipper. Other CPGs are looking at even more drastic changes, such as having products arrive at East Coast ports, even though the ultimate destination is a retail store in California. That real scenario is the fastest way for at least one company to maintain inventory to serve their customers</p>\n<p>While these strategies will help keep products on store shelves, they are not easy changes to implement and often have a negative impact on the shipper’s operational efficiency, at least in the early stages of adoption.</p>\n<h4><strong>Lifestyles have changed and consumer expectations are increasing</strong></h4>\n<p>While CPGs wrestle with these challenges, many consumers have changed their lifestyle and shopping habits. They count on e-commerce to have what they need and deliver it to their homes. This level of service may leave some consumers impatient with stock-outs or empty store shelves, especially combined with higher prices. And in reality, they do have other options – many items can be ordered online and in their hands within 24-48 hours.</p>\n<h4><strong>New challenges require new thinking and solutions</strong></h4>\n<p>To adapt to this new dynamic, CPGs must be able to quickly assess options and analyze potential gains versus risks. Having access to technology and market intelligence are basic building blocks. However, companies do not have the luxury of time to do exhaustive searches or requests for proposals.</p>\n<p>It is time to say goodbye to spreadsheets, manual bids done on an annual basis and make the most of the exciting new technologies that are reinventing many aspects of freight management, beginning with procurement.</p>\n<p>Is one bid a year agile enough to respond to a rapidly changing market? Do shippers or carriers have time to devote to many requests for proposals, which in the past have been very time-consuming? And can spread sheets and historical thinking “we’ve always done it this way” &#8211; offer the level of business intelligence needed for today’s supply chains?</p>\n<p>If even one of these answers is no, it may be time to <a href=\"https://emergemarket.com/\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\">reinvent the freight proposal process with Emerge</a>, a leading freight procurement platform that uses a combination of leading-edge technology, market intelligence and expertise in the freight industry to help companies reinvent the freight proposal process while revolutionizing many aspects of how freight is sourced and shipped. While challenging times may have led shippers to make a change, the benefits will last much longer than their current pain points.</p>\n<h5>About the Author</h5>\n<p><img fetchpriority=\"high\" decoding=\"async\" class=\"size-medium wp-image-12526 alignleft\" src=\"https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/DebraPhillips2-214x300.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"214\" height=\"300\" title=\"\" srcset=\"https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/DebraPhillips2-214x300.png 214w, https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/DebraPhillips2-732x1024.png 732w, https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/DebraPhillips2-768x1075.png 768w, https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/DebraPhillips2-1097x1536.png 1097w, https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/DebraPhillips2-600x840.png 600w, https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/DebraPhillips2.png 1286w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 214px) 100vw, 214px\" />Debra N. Phillips is Manager of Marketing for Emerge. She began her career in transportation in 1989 as Manager of Public Relations for Carolina Freight Carriers. Throughout her career, she has held leadership positions in companies including FedEx Freight, Penske, and MercuryGate.     "web_content": "<p>More than ever, consumers are thinking about sustainability and making lifestyle changes to protect the planet&#8217;s future. <a href=\"https://www.foodnavigator-usa.com/Article/2019/12/03/Nielsen-Which-sustainability-attributes-matter-most-to-consumers\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\">A 2019 Nielsen study found that 73% of global consumers are willing to change their consumption patterns to reduce their environmental impact. </a>This includes thinking about sustainability when making online purchases along with how and when those purchases will arrive.</p>\n<p>Trucks, planes, ships, and trains carry billions of tons of cargo each year and <a href=\"https://climate.mit.edu/ask-mit/how-can-carbon-emissions-freight-be-reduced\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\">contribute 8% of global greenhouse gas emissions. The number rises to 11% if you include emissions from warehouses and ports</a>. Retailers and manufacturers feel increased pressure from consumers and governments to become greener with their transportation and delivery methods. Big brands are setting aggressive goals to appeal to environmentally conscious consumers and to meet their governments&#8217; carbon-neutral targets.</p>\n<p>The United Nations climate conference held in Glasgow (COP26) created the Glasgow Climate Pact, signed by 200 countries, various business leaders and environmental activists. Two of the five COP26 announcements will impact the supply chain industry, especially delivery operations.</p>\n<p>How can you measure and reduce your delivery carbon footprint? How can you incorporate sustainability into first, mid and last-mile delivery?</p>\n<h4><strong>The Ripple Effects of COP26 in Supply Chain Delivery </strong></h4>\n<p>As consumers increase their online purchases, the decarbonization of delivery transport has become a new challenge. Brands are beginning to reinvent their business models to handle products while being sensitive to sustainability goals. Transport decarbonization impacts last-mile delivery in logistics and the first and mid-mile of supply chain operations.</p>\n<p>The majority of consumer goods move by road transport. Sectors that focus on consumers, like retail, e-commerce, big &amp; bulky, courier express, and parcel will face the most significant impact of new decarbonization goals. How will brands and enterprises create and measure sustainable goals to reduce their carbon footprints across all delivery phases?</p>\n<h4><strong>FarEye’s Intelligent Supply Chain Platform Helps Brands Achieve Sustainability Goals</strong></h4>\n<p>While some 3PL carriers associated with top-tier brands and in-house logistics teams of global brands have access to tools to measure CO2 emissions accurately, most enterprises lack systems to capture the carbon emission readings of their fleets. Each business has unique supply chain delivery operations and the associated carbon emission struggles.</p>\n<p>FarEye’s Intelligent Supply Chain Platform helps enterprises fast-track their <a href=\"https://www.getfareye.com/sustainability/\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\">sustainability</a> goals using a science-based CO2 reduction approach. Key sustainability capabilities help brands and enterprises achieve sustainable goals across first, mid and last-mile delivery.</p>\n<p>FarEye’s sustainability dashboard allows customers to track various Key Performance Indicators tied to carbon emissions. Enterprises can access insights such as the amount of C02 emissions per trips and shipments and identify routes that contribute to maximum and minimal carbon emissions. FarEye’s Platform also helps route planning for green vehicles and long-haul trucks. The dashboard is flexible to accommodate the needs of all businesses, large and small, across industries like manufacturing, retail, e-commerce and express couriers. The supply chain industry is at the center of this green transition. Enterprises that proactively optimize supply chain operations to reduce carbon emissions will have a significant competitive advantage to attract new investments and gain the goodwill of new-age consumers.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://letstalksupplychain.com/episode249/\">Hear more about sustainability and reducing carbon emissions across first, mid and last-mile deliveries today on Let’s Talk Supply Chain.</a></p>\n<h4><strong>About the Author</strong></h4>\n<p><img fetchpriority=\"high\" decoding=\"async\" class=\" wp-image-12467 alignleft\" src=\"https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/delivery-management-300x201.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"315\" height=\"212\" title=\"\" srcset=\"https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/delivery-management-300x201.png 300w, https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/delivery-management.png 450w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 315px) 100vw, 315px\" />As CEO, Kushal Nahata is responsible for driving the vision, strategy, and growth at FarEye.     "web_content": "<p>The workforce is only expected to grow 4% in the next decade. Compare that with the 1970s at 30% or the 2000s at 9%, and it&#8217;s easy to see why we&#8217;re seeing more alarmist headlines about The Great Resignation. For the first time in well, modern history, there are one and a half jobs open for hire for every unemployed American. At virtually any other point, all employers had to do was post a job online or help wanted sign and wait for the applicants. Now, everything is changing.</p>\n<p>In response to a pandemic, professionals across generational gaps are reevaluating the why and how behind their work. An unprecedented talent shortage is clashing abruptly with a wave of Baby Boomer retirements. There&#8217;s a powerful seachange coming to corporate culture and work-life ethos, driven by a millennial-dominated workforce that&#8217;s been working through a global pandemic for two years.</p>\n<p>They don&#8217;t want to hear about hustle culture anymore. In fact, <a href=\"https://sloanreview.mit.edu/article/toxic-culture-is-driving-the-great-resignation/\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\">according to a recent study</a>, burning out and overwhelming employees and creating a toxic working culture are a couple of the most common reasons employees are leaving their jobs in droves.</p>\n<p>The changing talent landscape is reframing how we traditionally think about outsourcing.</p>\n<h2>Empower your teams with outside expertise.</h2>\n<p>Employers are experiencing what Forbes labeled a &#8220;<a href=\"https://www.forbes.com/sites/jackkelly/2021/10/01/baby-boomers-are-leaving-the-workforce-to-live-their-best-lives-in-a-silver-tsunami-great-retirement-trend/?sh=35ba2c65260b\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\">Silver Tsunami</a>.&#8221; Almost 30 million Baby Boomers left the workplace in the third quarter of 2020 amidst the pandemic&#8217;s darkest days. The COVID-19 pandemic has been a driving force for the mass exodus of Boomers born between 1946 and 1964 to call it quits and put their health and wellbeing first. Many organizations are having trouble filling some of their most senior positions or eliminating them with so many leaving.</p>\n<p>That leaves serious knowledge gaps in different areas, including supply chain, operations, IT, sales, and marketing. Bringing outside experts in these areas can help your organization achieve a competitive edge while keeping your full-time team members inundated and educated on the latest best practices and approaches.</p>\n<h2>Put out the burnout.</h2>\n<p>As hiring becomes more challenging, running leaner businesses might sound attractive to employers looking to maximize profit margins. However,  attrition is expensive. Organizations must avoid burning out employees who can easily find another job with a better work-life balance—because they will. Identifying areas where your workforce can use support can help you support growing pains while empowering your talent to focus on what they know best—your customers.</p>\n<p>It&#8217;s also essential to focus on building an engaged, connected workforce backed by a vibrant, positive company culture. When you&#8217;re navigating supply chain shortages, an agile, competitive, digital market, and running all the basic business operations through an ongoing talent gap, that&#8217;s hard to do.</p>\n<p>Partnering with the right outsourcing organization can help you and your company leaders focus on keeping your existing workforce engaged and involved in your day-to-day work and company culture.</p>\n<h2>Take some pressure off of your middle management team.</h2>\n<p>Without a steady flow of new talent ready if and when an employee resigns, there&#8217;s a growing amount of anxiety among hiring managers juggling daily people operations, keeping teams across organizations in sync and aligned, and trying to retain talent. You might have a hard time filling new or existing positions quickly, and that&#8217;s where the right outsourcing partner can help you support your existing team members while you grow.</p>\n<p>Identifying areas where your management team can use support can help optimize business processes and let them focus more on people management and retention. Implementing the right outsourcing strategy can enable you to scale your workforce on a realistic timeline—no matter the job market conditions.</p>\n<h2><strong>The talent shortage has only started. How will you do more with less?</strong></h2>\n<p>Experts predict a <a href=\"https://www.economicmodeling.com/video/sansdemic-too-much-work-too-little-people/\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\">sansdemic</a> for decades to come—literally translated as a shortage of people. It&#8217;s time to find strategic approaches to supporting your existing workforce to keep them and your business thriving. Turnover can be costly and devastating for small-to-medium-sized enterprises. Being able to flex and scale outside support across your business and supply chain operations can keep your organization moving through disruption and into the future—fast and strategically.</p>\n<h2><em>Ready to rethink your outsourcing strategy?</em></h2>\n<p>Unlike most offshoring partners, at Zenov, we offer a variety of services backed by a North-American-based executive office and staff.     "summary": null,

    "related_articles": [],
    "web_content": "<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Snow in Texas. Wildfires, tsunamis and heatwaves— all of this plus shipping containers, air freight and exports being sent and seen around the world.</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">That makes anyone wonder exactly how much carbon dioxide is emitted into our air per gallon of diesel burned? Well, the U.S. EPA says 22.461 pounds. As it stands, climate change is an inevitable challenge the supply chain faces.</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Though dealing with climate change is unavoidable, supply chain companies and industry professionals have an undeniable chance to combat its effects. But tree-planting events, recycling programs and sustainable packing strategies are just a mere starting point. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Reducing your emissions is key. End-to-end visibility is key. Not only for eco-friendly practices but for your bottom line. But you can’t, no matter how hard you try, reduce emissions unless you measure it. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">You can monitor the pulse of your supply chain emissions using tools like the FourKites sustainability dashboard. Putting a plan in place to reduce emissions should be a central part of any green strategy.</span></p>\n<h3><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Going Green, But on a Global Level</span></h3>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Our planet is getting smaller. Not physically, but we’re able to communicate differently, easier.  Which should make it easy for countries to come together and make an impact. In fact, European companies were surveyed by </span><a href=\"https://www.fourkites.com/resources/state-of-the-european-supply-chain-logistics-sustainability-and-visibility-report-2022/\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Fourkites</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">, a leader in supply chain visibility. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The data found that business leaders there are already getting a head start on their sustainability plans. </span></p>\n<ul>\n<li style=\"font-weight: 400;\" aria-level=\"1\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Over 80% indicated they were increasing or maintaining their sustainability commitments.</span></li>\n<li style=\"font-weight: 400;\" aria-level=\"1\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">About 50% of respondents cited real-time supply chain visibility data as an essential part of identifying and hitting sustainability objectives.</span></li>\n<li style=\"font-weight: 400;\" aria-level=\"1\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">41% of respondents have trouble measuring their impact on sustainability.</span></li>\n</ul>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Some say,</span><i><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> “green business is good business”</span></i><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">. It couldn’t be more true. We’re predicting that those who take sustainability seriously now, will still be in operation and making revenue in 2042. Those who chose to ignore the issue will soon find themselves lost in a figurative congested port.</span></p>\n<h3><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Supply Chain Collaboration for Sustainability</span></h3>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">There was an underlying theme at the 2021 United Nations Climate Change Conference. The message? Sustainability isn’t only assigned to political leaders. Companies need to step up and take charge. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">As a response to this and climate change, the International Maritime Organization (IMO) has ordered that all vessels reduce emissions by half, and by the year 2050. Several fuel-efficient programs would need to be implemented over the next decade to meet these goals, because ships have a 20- to 25-year lifetime. It&#8217;s possible, but the required technologies would need to be honed in faster, at a higher scale, and at a lower cost.</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">With various kinds of micro-mobility and zero-emission (ZE) cars, buses, and light commercial vehicles, the decarbonization of transportation has come a long way in many countries. Despite this, medium- and heavy-duty trucks (MDTs and HDTs) have been lagging behind. Currently, road freight accounts for 53 percent of global trade-related emissions, and if current trends continue, that&#8217;s going to rise to 56 percent by 2050—right when IMO plans to half their emission outputs. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Despite recent technological advancements that have put a low-carbon truck future within reach, increasing collaboration across the value chain will be necessary to succeed. A new initiative by the World Economic Forum (WEF) called Road Freight Zero (RFZ) aims to help companies join forces and develop solutions. Participants include manufacturers of consumer goods, logistics companies, fleet operators, energy, technology, and infrastructure firms, innovators, finance companies, academic institutions, and civil society organizations.</span></p>\n<h3><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Multimodal Solution</span></h3>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">So what is the solution supply chain leaders are so badly seeking for sustainability efforts?</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">According to the same FourKites survey, 67% of respondents said the biggest struggle they had was end-to-end tracking of their goals.</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Luckily, Fourkites’ visibility platform provides the solution to reduce emissions and your carbon footprint, giving you the ability to understand and identify your waste through data.</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Customers can use the platform to </span><a href=\"https://www.fourkites.com/press/fourkites-introduces-supply-chain-sustainability-dashboard/\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">see the environmental impact</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> of their supply chain operations.</span></p>\n<h3><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Keep Your Supply Chain Business Going for 20 More Years with Sustainability Plans</span></h3>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Emissions are a part of supply chain. It’s unavoidable. But since it’s easier to collaborate with and partner for the greater, greener good, reducing emissions from supply chain operations is possible.</span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">You can now be a part of the global green supply chain! </span><a href=\"https://www.fourkites.com/sustainability-summit-2022/\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The world’s largest virtual event that focuses on the supply chain environmental impact is happening SOON!</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> You can tune into engaging panel discussions, presentations, and perspectives all on sustainability. We’ll be there! Will you?</span></p>\n",

    "uuid": "b74ffcd6-22cc-46a4-b2c6-d53cea3b8996",
    "post_id": 12138,
    "type": "blogs",
    "title": "Attract Top Talent — And Retain It — With a High-Involvement Culture",
    "slug": "attract-top-talent-and-retain-it-with-a-high-involvement-culture",
    "date": "2022-02-01T04:00:17",
    "summary": null,
    "main_points": null,
    "recent_news": null,
    "related_articles": [],
    "web_content": "<p>In a recent episode of the Let’s Talk Supply Chain podcast, I spoke about tech and sustainability’s influence on the freight industry and acquiring and retaining purpose-driven talent, the latter of which is my bread and butter.</p>\n<p>My people operations experience has taught me the powerful impact culture has on a company’s success. That’s the mindset I bring to my current role as senior vice president of people at <a href=\"https://www.flockfreight.com/home-page/\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\">Flock Freight</a>, a <a href=\"https://www.flockfreight.com/about-us/careers/technology/\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\">technology company</a> that’s reducing waste and inefficiency by reinventing the supply chain. First to market with advanced algorithms that enable supply chain optimization by pooling shipments, Flock Freight creates a new standard of service for <a href=\"https://www.flockfreight.com/freight-shipping/\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\">shippers</a>, increases revenue for <a href=\"https://www.flockfreight.com/freight-carriers/\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\">carriers</a>, and eliminates the impact of carbon emissions through shared truckload service.</p>\n<p>Speedily transitioning from underdog startup to billion-dollar tech enterprise, Flock Freight gives me the unique opportunity to work with an ever-growing team that’s fundamentally changing the way freight moves. As we embark on a second year of doubling our workforce, it’s especially critical that we attract and retain the right talent, and preserve certain aspects of our evolving culture while welcoming unfamiliar changes.</p>\n<h2>Recruiting Culture Adds</h2>\n<p>Building a stellar team isn’t just about attracting the best candidates; it’s about hiring the right candidates for the right reasons. That’s where “culture add” versus “culture fit” comes into play.</p>\n<p>Culture fit is the practice of hiring candidates who look, think, act, and have similar backgrounds to your current team. It assumes your company has everything figured out and that all new hires need to do is fit in. Culture add, on the other hand, involves recognizing an opportunity to welcome candidates of other experiences and ideas. These additions may not have gone to the same schools or are not the same age as your current employees, but their diverse perspectives can enrich your culture.</p>\n<p>At Flock Freight, our customers and carrier partners are incredibly diverse, so the more diversity we have on our team, the better we are at understanding our stakeholders, anticipating their needs, and forming effective communication. If we can broaden our culture, we can broaden our stakeholder impact.</p>\n<h2>Fostering a High-Involvement Culture</h2>\n<p>In order to sustainably grow our team, we must retain employees and keep them happy. Fostering a positive work culture is the key to achieving that. Culture isn’t just up to human resources or the executive suite — it’s the employees who are in charge of employee culture.</p>\n<p>A high-involvement culture encourages and empowers employees to be active, conscious participants in employee culture. Employees should have avenues to be culture champions within organizations, and those avenues should have support from leadership and a budget behind them. At Flock Freight, this takes the form of five employee-run Impact teams focused on diversity and inclusion, the environment, employee engagement, community engagement, and philanthropy.</p>\n<p>As <a href=\"https://www.flockfreight.com/about-us/careers/\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\">Flock Freight grows</a>, our culture evolves organically, and as a people operations team, it’s our responsibility to help shape and guide it. We do that in part by recognizing and rewarding employees who exhibit our five core values: All in, Do the right thing, Empower others, Be agile, and Think big.</p>\n<p>I encourage other companies who want to foster a positive culture to find the people within your organization who care about it. Don&#8217;t look to your HR team — they care about it by definition — look to your other teams and get those folks to share their time and expertise. Engaged employees will often come up with better thoughts and solutions than any HR team. Also, gauge how your employees feel about your culture by utilizing surveys — an invaluable tool every company should use. Ask your employees how you’re doing, and when you find areas of opportunity in your company culture, go to employee groups to source solutions — don’t just wait for your HR department to fix it.</p>\n<h2>About the Author</h2>\n<p><img fetchpriority=\"high\" decoding=\"async\" class=\"size-medium wp-image-12142 alignleft\" src=\"https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/01/Melina-Fairleigh-Headshot-Square-Sandy-Athniel-300x292.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"300\" height=\"292\" title=\"\" srcset=\"https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/01/Melina-Fairleigh-Headshot-Square-Sandy-Athniel-300x292.jpg 300w, https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/01/Melina-Fairleigh-Headshot-Square-Sandy-Athniel-1024x998.jpg 1024w, https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/01/Melina-Fairleigh-Headshot-Square-Sandy-Athniel-768x748.jpg 768w, https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/01/Melina-Fairleigh-Headshot-Square-Sandy-Athniel-1536x1496.jpg 1536w, https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/01/Melina-Fairleigh-Headshot-Square-Sandy-Athniel-2048x1995.jpg 2048w, https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/01/Melina-Fairleigh-Headshot-Square-Sandy-Athniel-600x585.jpg 600w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 300px) 100vw, 300px\" /></p>\n<p>Melina Fairleigh is the senior vice president of people at Flock Freight, a technology company that’s reducing waste and inefficiency by reinventing the supply chain. She has over 20 years of people operations experience in various industries, including tech and food retail. Fostering a positive work culture is what Melina does best.     "web_content": "<p>I know what you’re thinking. You’ve just gone through 2 years of hell trying to plug the holes in your supply chain through the disruption that will go unnamed, and now I’m talking about new technology? You’ve heard of “low-code” applications over the past couple years, but what exactly does that mean in supply chain and why is it essential? In any case, you’ve already committed millions for EPR upgrades that will not only consume most of your IT budget, but also keep your IT staff fully occupied for the rest of the year, so low code is not on your radar. This is a mistake.</p>\n<p>The truth is, low code applications are already all over yours, and everyone else’s, company. In the past, it’s been called “shadow IT”—you know, the applications that actually run your business. Many of these applications are run using what is called the Lingua Franca of business—Excel. As you undoubtedly know (as well as over 1B other users), there’s simply no better data environment (a grid of cells) on which you can model out virtually any supply chain, or other, business application. Forecasts, trackers, pricing, inventory, promotions, projects, production plans—the list of applications is endless.</p>\n<p>Your “citizen developers,” otherwise known as your subject matter experts who know your business and its processes, have relied on Excel for years. Supply chain is no exception. In fact, 68% of companies with supply chain operations use Excel spreadsheets as the primary technology for planning, despite the fact that 92% of these companies already have supply chain planning applications (2021 Supply Chain Insights Global Conference). And, this continues even with the familiar problems with Excel – emailing or file shares, silos of data, error prone, who made the last change, what version are we on, is the data in the Excel file accurate, etc. Given that Gartner predicts that by 2024, more than 65% of application development activity will be low code, wouldn’t it be nice to find a low-code application platform that leverages all this process IP that you already have in Excel?</p>\n<p>Enter <a href=\"https://www.boardwalktech.com/products/planning-apps#contact-us\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\">Boardwalktech</a>. For over 15 years, we’ve been working with Fortune 500 companies helping them scale applications they run manually in Excel today with a patented, cloud Digital Ledger database platform. With an authoring platform that runs in Excel and uses your Excel-based process IP “as-is” (yes, including formula logic), you can go from manually collaborating via email or a file share to automatically sharing cell-level changes via an “Excel” cloud database. All this, while retaining the flexibility of Excel and gaining the power and scalability of a cloud database. Imagine, being able to share data from inside Excel with other users with a click. To have data from one Excel process flow into another. To gain visibility across all your Excel-based activity. To understand how all this data changes over time to power more insightful machine learning and predictive analytics. While at the same time, reducing your time spent chasing data by 75% helping you get to the right decision, faster. And, there’s more. The Boardwalk Digital Ledger works with unstructured data bringing all your enterprise data together via a powerful control tower.</p>\n<p>Just think about how many applications are run manually in Excel today in your company—it’s time to turn this into a competitive advantage. Only by using a low-code application platform that directly leverages your Excel-based process IP without forcing you to recode it into another application, can you then be part of the 450 million low-code apps Microsoft says will be built over the next 5 years. The time to start is today.</p>\n<p>Get started today by joining our spreadsheet challenge.     "uuid": "2ac0ad73-66b3-4591-b85e-0393324e3688",

    "type": "blogs",
    "title": "How freight forwarding technology improves efficiency and transparency in supply chain operations",
    "slug": "how-freight-forwarding-technology-improves-efficiency-and-transparency-in-supply-chain-operations",
    "date": "2021-12-14T04:00:50",
    "summary": null,
    "main_points": null,
    "recent_news": null,
    "related_articles": [],
    "web_content": "<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">In a recent discussion on the </span><a href=\"https://letstalksupplychain.com/\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Let’s Talk Supply Chain</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> podcast, Shabsie Levy talked about the pivotal role of technology in improving the efficiency of supply chain operations. In early 2019, Levy started </span><a href=\"https://shifl.com/\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Shifl</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">, a digital freight forwarding platform that leverages technology integration to navigate bottlenecks, reduce delays, increase transparency, and improve visibility across the supply chain. Combining the digital automation experience with personnel representative support in multiple locations across the globe, </span><a href=\"https://shifl.com/\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Shifl</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> seamlessly supports small and big customers in their freight operations. Its future vision is to create a freight ecosystem that enables its customers to do business without worrying about logistics management.</span></p>\n<p><b>How Shifl helps customers stay connected with updates</b></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Levy’s previous experiences in the industry helped him gain insight into bottlenecks such as delays in receiving important shipping updates that slow down operations. Shifl has now evolved into a solution that bridges the gap between the customer’s need to stay updated and real-time updates from ground zero. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Shifl provides its customers with the latest status updates at every step along the way, from the time the purchase order is placed to when the shipment is delivered. Using live statuses gathered from tracking systems, their software helps customers stay updated with the latest piece of information. By doing this, Shifl empowers its customers to make informed decisions and operate their businesses efficiently, even during challenging times. </span></p>\n<p><b>How Shifl’s flexible payment options help customers stay afloat during tough times</b></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">One of </span><a href=\"https://shifl.com/\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Shifl’s</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> most unique offerings is that it allows its customers to pay with a credit card without imposing processing fees. When shipping rates go up, smaller businesses often struggle to arrange the sudden cash flow required to keep their businesses going. The burden of shouldering credit processing fees along with sky-high freight costs puts added pressure on them. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Providing flexible payment options to customers lets them continue their operations without having to incur extra costs to keep going. Customers also receive the added flexibility to float an average of 40-45 days between multiple credit cards. This gives them ample support to keep their business going till things ease and the cash flow comes in. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Levy also pointed out how they went the extra mile to help their customers by talking to insurance companies to get some customers approved for higher credit limits during the last two years when the industry saw some of the highest container rates.</span></p>\n<p><b>How technology integration works at Shifl</b></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">At the heart of </span><a href=\"https://shifl.com/\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Shifl’s</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> core operations is its aim to reduce the disconnect in the industry and harness technology to integrate various systems. Levy explained how the platform functions as a central hub of information. APIs allow it to integrate data from third-party systems into its database and give out data to feed into a different system. For instance, Shifl has partnered with Terminal 49 to receive accurate container and ocean freight tracking data that it can relay to its customers. Additionally, it uses this information to create automation tools and strengthen its integration with third-party systems. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">This being said, Levy and his team still have to overcome a lot of challenges to make Shifl a full-service solution. Smaller companies don’t possess API technology even today. Handling complex shipment scenarios such as less-container-load (LCL) shipments are complicated. There are a lot of such scenarios where 100% automation is still not possible. In such cases, </span><a href=\"https://shifl.com/\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Shifl </span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">uses manual intervention to sustain. With its manual tracking team constantly gathering updates, Shifl continues to serve its customers across complex scenarios.</span></p>\n<p><b>How future technology integrations at Shifl will help improve customer experience</b></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Alongside the services it offers, Shifl continues to grow with Levy and their team accelerating ideas and turning their future visions for the company to reality. Levy’s ultimate vision is to create a complete freight ecosystem that lets its customers do their business without worrying about logistics management. In the coming months, Levy and his team are adding tools with greater features for its customers to forecast industry trends, have a detailed look inside inventories, and integrate eCommerce with their platform. </span></p>\n<h2>About the Author</h2>\n<p><img fetchpriority=\"high\" decoding=\"async\" class=\"size-medium wp-image-10881 alignleft\" src=\"https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/12/technology-integration-with-shifl-300x200.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"300\" height=\"200\" title=\"\" srcset=\"https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/12/technology-integration-with-shifl-300x200.jpg 300w, https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/12/technology-integration-with-shifl-1024x682.jpg 1024w, https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/12/technology-integration-with-shifl-768x512.jpg 768w, https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/12/technology-integration-with-shifl-600x400.jpg 600w, https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/12/technology-integration-with-shifl.jpg 1280w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 300px) 100vw, 300px\" />Shabsie is the Founder and CEO of Shifl. He has over a decade of experience in the international supply chain industry along with an extensive background in software and digital innovation. Shifl was founded with expertise of the past and a vision of the future to propel global shipping into the cloud age. With an international presence together with its advanced software, Shifl streamlines your supply chain while eliminating inefficiencies, resulting in transparency and reduced costs.</p>\n<div class=\"freebirdFormviewerViewNumberedItemContainer\" role=\"listitem\">\n<div class=\"freebirdFormviewerViewItemsItemItem\" data-required=\"true\" data-input=\"L9xHkb\" data-item-id=\"1609135432\">\n<div class=\"freebirdFormviewerViewItemsItemItemHeader\">\n<div class=\"freebirdFormviewerViewItemsItemItemTitleDescContainer\">\n<div class=\"freebirdFormviewerViewItemsItemItemTitleContainer\"></div>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n",

    "uuid": "521bb743-0072-4a28-98e0-6a7c84a444b3",
    "post_id": 10868,
    "type": "blogs",
    "title": "Going Beyond: FourKites Expands Ocean Capabilities to Drive End-to-End Supply Chain Visibility",
    "slug": "going-beyond-fourkites-expands-ocean-capabilities-to-drive-end-to-end-supply-chain-visibility",
    "date": "2021-12-13T18:04:02",
    "summary": null,
    "main_points": null,
    "recent_news": null,
    "related_articles": [],
    "web_content": "<p>It’s been a difficult two years for supply chain and, as we head into 2022, it’s clear that things aren’t going to get easier any time soon. The one constant has been disruption, and we’ve seen it everywhere — from computer chip shortages to a truck driver employment crisis. But there’s one area that has everyone’s attention, and that’s shipping.</p>\n<p>The level of port congestion has been unprecedented, as has the two-fold issue with containers: the sheer volume we’ve seen either <a href=\"https://www.fourkites.com/blogs/ocean-shipping-in-turmoil-3-lessons-from-zim-kingston-disruption/\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\">going overboard</a> or lying uncollected or abandoned in ports across the world. And this has, of course, led to higher costs for companies as well as consumers and, increasingly, empty store shelves.</p>\n<p>Managing the current shipping crisis has become priority number one, with President Joe Biden announcing <a href=\"https://cheddar.com/media/breaking-down-the-24-7-port-of-la-deal-and-supply-chain-bottleneck\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\">24/7 operations</a> at the Port of Los Angeles and the Port of Long Beach in an effort to clear the backlog in the run-up to the holidays.</p>\n<p>I truly hope it helps, but I question if simply throwing more manpower at the crisis is the right thing to do. It feels like trying to reattach a limb with a band-aid! I don’t think the solution lies in working harder; it’s about working smarter.</p>\n<p>FourKites, the world’s leading real-time supply chain visibility platform, is bringing that ethos to the industry. The company recently announced <a href=\"https://www.fourkites.com/press/fourkites-expands-its-market-leading-ocean-visibility-platform-with-industry-first-dynamic-eta%ef%b8%8f-for-ocean-shipping-and-new-tools-to-manage-demurrage-and-detention/\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\">AI-powered enhancements to its Dynamic Ocean solution</a>, enabling it to provide ETAs that are up to 40% more accurate than carrier-generated ETAs. Up to 40%!   that could have at the ports. That increased accuracy can help prevent port congestion and better predict waiting times, reducing air pollution and fuel consumption. It can help better allocate resources and avoid conflicts which, in turn, could help with the current labor shortages. And ultimately, this will lead to increased efficiency and transparency in the global supply chain. Sounds good, right?</p>\n<p>And to support their Dynamic Ocean solution, FourKites have also rolled out a new suite of demurrage and detention tools that provide customers with an early warning solution and actionable insights, replacing the manual and/or spreadsheet-driven approaches used by most shippers. And if you’re a regular listener to the podcast, you’ll know just how necessary it is to get shippers out of Excel and into the future!</p>\n<p>These new capabilities mean that FourKites now provides <em>the</em> most advanced and robust solution on the market for <a href=\"https://www.fourkites.com/platform/ocean-freight-visibility/\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\">real-time and predictive ocean visibility</a>, exception management and cost controls, giving shippers the powerful capabilities to effectively manage and mitigate rising transportation costs during a time of constant upheaval.</p>\n<p>This all goes to show that visibility is a vital piece in helping to solve the supply chain puzzle — not a passing trend. Gartner, the leading research and advisory firm who <a href=\"https://letstalksupplychain.com/fourkites-continues-to-push-the-envelope-as-its-named-a-leader-in-gartners-magic-quadrant-for-real-time-transportation-visibility-platforms/\">named FourKites a Leader</a> in its Spring 2021 report, said that visibility is a top priority for supply chain leaders. And that demand for supply chain visibility has continued to increase in all modes, including requests for more insight and connection across international and multimodal shipments.</p>\n<p>Because visibility isn’t just about looking on a map and seeing dots that represent your freight in transit. That insight and connection needs to go completely end-to-end — and ideally integrated into one single platform — to achieve the impact and improvements we all need. Businesses need to see where their containers are at port, in the yard, warehouse, stores and beyond. By gaining high levels of multimodal visibility, businesses can benefit in so many ways, from achieving higher levels of ETA accuracy and optimizing fuel consumption, to mitigating transportation risks and reducing carbon footprint. The importance of multimodal visibility cannot be overstated.</p>\n<p>Gartner’s claims that demand for this level of supply chain visibility is increasing is reinforced by data from the FourKites platform. Over the last 12 months, FourKites has seen 450% growth in ocean loads tracked, and 40% growth quarter over quarter. Since launching Dynamic Ocean in April 2021, which covers 98% of global ocean shipments, 100% of terminals in North America and the majority of terminals in Europe, FourKites has seen a 50% increase in ocean visibility customers, including Yara International, International Forest Products and Zebra Technologies.</p>\n<p>So as demand increases, as well as disruption, it’s essential to have innovative and forward-thinking brands like FourKites. Their new Dynamic Ocean enhancements have come in direct response to the shipping crisis. It makes me proud to see a business that is so committed to bringing the industry into the future and to delivering solutions that make life easier for all of us.</p>\n<p>End-to-end visibility ultimately has the potential to create a more sustainable future and ensure a much smoother ride through the next, inevitable, set of disruptions.</p>\n<p>&nbsp;</p>\n<p>Find out more about FourKites’ <a href=\"https://letstalksupplychain.com/fourkites-combines-innovation-and-collaboration/\">approach to collaboration and innovation</a>, and their <a href=\"https://letstalksupplychain.com/collaboration-meets-visibility-why-fourkites-recent-funding-success-brings-supply-chain-one-step-closer-to-the-future/\">recent funding success</a>.</p>\n",

    "uuid": "ee733e40-0220-40b5-92cf-ea1ee6be71db",
    "post_id": 10760,
    "type": "blogs",
    "title": "Preparing for 2022: Looking beyond recovery",
    "slug": "preparing-for-2022-looking-beyond-recovery",
    "date": "2021-12-06T14:53:20",
    "summary": null,
    "main_points": null,
    "recent_news": null,

    "web_content": "<p>In the past two years, multiple lockdowns, port congestion and other such challenges have resulted in supply chain chaos worldwide.</p>\n<p>The industry has been facing unprecedented challenges, which are likely to continue well into 2022. In that light, here are 5 ways companies can prepare for the coming year.</p>\n<h2>1. Embrace digital transformation</h2>\n<p>Using the right technology, you can get a holistic view of your supply chain so you can act proactively, mitigate risks and make more informed decisions. The time is now to adapt by embracing digital transformation. And this doesn’t have to cost an exorbitant amount &#8211; the technology to help already exists, and is both cost-effective and easy to implement.</p>\n<h2>2. Diversify your ecosystem</h2>\n<p>Though unfortunate, it’s common for disruptions such as natural disasters, port closures, product shortages &#8211; and nowadays COVID variants &#8211; to pop up and negatively affect your supply chain. To enable flexibility and minimize disruptions to your supply chain you should diversify. Have a supply chain that involves multiple suppliers and partners across a range of local, regional, and global locations to support operations.</p>\n<h2>3. Sustainable sourcing</h2>\n<p>The fashion industry is responsible for about 10% of the world’s carbon emissions. COP26 has highlighted the need for the industry to be more sustainable. We imagine this will be a huge focus in the next year. Fashion companies will need to know the provenance of their products and how they are made. Sustainable sourcing will also be a key priority. With regulators and consumers demanding more transparency, companies who are proactive will have a competitive edge.</p>\n<h2>4. Overcome silo mentality</h2>\n<p>The apparel industry is notoriously opaque and fragmented. In order to achieve true transparency, businesses and the wider industry have to break down silos. Without information-sharing amongst key departments in a company,  it’s difficult for any business to have a complete picture and act quickly to take advantage of new opportunities.</p>\n<h2>5. Measure what matters</h2>\n<p>There’s a significant amount of data held across systems. Technology can help consolidate and analyze this data to provide powerful insights. For example, they can help identify inefficiencies in their supply chain, or drive performance against KPIs by learning from historic trends.</p>\n<p>&nbsp;</p>\n<h2>About the Author</h2>\n<p><img fetchpriority=\"high\" decoding=\"async\" class=\"size-medium wp-image-10764 alignleft\" src=\"https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/12/serai-trade-300x298.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"300\" height=\"298\" title=\"\" srcset=\"https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/12/serai-trade-300x298.jpg 300w, https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/12/serai-trade-150x150.jpg 150w, https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/12/serai-trade-60x60.jpg 60w, https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/12/serai-trade-600x596.jpg 600w, https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/12/serai-trade-100x100.jpg 100w, https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/12/serai-trade.jpg 611w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 300px) 100vw, 300px\" /><a href=\"https://www.linkedin.com/in/lindseyhermes\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\">Lindsey Hermes</a> is a professional in the digital B2B world.</p>\n",

Instead, our software provides the tools to understand the story it’s telling you. But more importantly, Sifted helps you visualize how that story changes when you model different operational tactics. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Smarter shipping </span><b>is</b><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> the future Sifted can promise. </span></p>\n<h4><b>Visibility Is Just The First Step</b></h4>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">It’s crucial for your business’s success to see your shipping data in one place. You need visibility into your operations.</span></p>\n<p><i><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">But what do you do with that data? </span></i></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Data on its </span><i><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">own</span></i><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> doesn’t help you figure out your problem areas, or where you can change up a service mix or two to better match your needs. </span></p>\n<h4><b>Cost Optimization Is Where You Make Change</b></h4>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">That’s where the Sifted Score comes into play. They could drop you if you start making demands.</span></p>\n<p><i><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">What can you do instead?</span></i></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Look </span><b>inwards</b><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> and focus on what&#8217;s happening within the four corners of your own data. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">You </span><i><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">can</span></i><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> take control of your data, gain visibility, and optimize operations yourself with logistics intelligence.
