  {
    "uuid": "c472b98c-68a9-445e-8582-dc21792b71da",
    "post_id": 4923,
    "type": "blogs",
    "title": "5 Steps to Developing a Smashing Influencer Marketing Approach",
    "slug": "developing-a-smashing-influencer-marketing-strategy",
    "date": "2021-04-27T08:36:02",
    "summary": null,
    "main_points": null,
    "recent_news": null,
    "related_articles": [],
    "web_content": "<p><img fetchpriority=\"high\" decoding=\"async\" class=\"aligncenter wp-image-4926 size-full\" src=\"https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/04/top-rank-influencer.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"758\" height=\"428\" title=\"\" srcset=\"https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/04/top-rank-influencer.png 758w, https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/04/top-rank-influencer-600x339.png 600w, https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/04/top-rank-influencer-300x169.png 300w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 758px) 100vw, 758px\" /></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">When you think of influencer marketing, your first thought is likely of B2C celebrity endorsements where a famous person is paid to promote something. Those types of traditional commercial deals exist, sure, but they’re only a small portion of the real, everyday impact of influencer marketing. Think about supply chain: are you more likely to check out a product if it’s been recommended by an industry expert like Sarah Barnes-Humphrey?</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">According to the recent State of B2B Influencer Marketing Research Report, 63% of marketers agree that their marketing would have better results if it included a B2B influencer marketing program. The question then becomes: how do I develop this sort of program and make it work for my business? </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">There are five steps to setting up a successful influencer marketing strategy, and I’ll be detailing all of them for you below. These steps will work for any industry, but we’ll be paying special attention to their impact on the supply chain industry in this post. I’ve affectionately labeled this strategy the SMASH strategy thanks to its ability to smash through stagnancy and help businesses push forward.</span></p>\n<ol>\n<li><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> Set-up</span></li>\n</ol>\n<p><b>First is set-up. </b><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The foundation of any successful marketing strategy is information. This portion of the process is about gathering that information and organizing it in a way that is understandable and actionable. What questions do you need to answer about your business before you can move forward to the next step? Let’s review:</span></p>\n<ul>\n<li style=\"font-weight: 400;\" aria-level=\"1\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Who is my target audience?</span></li>\n<li style=\"font-weight: 400;\" aria-level=\"1\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">What are my main pain points?</span></li>\n<li style=\"font-weight: 400;\" aria-level=\"1\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">What are my current solutions for those pain points?</span></li>\n<li style=\"font-weight: 400;\" aria-level=\"1\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Which topics are most relevant to my unique industry?</span></li>\n<li style=\"font-weight: 400;\" aria-level=\"1\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Who are my main competitors?</span></li>\n<li style=\"font-weight: 400;\" aria-level=\"1\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">What are my business goals?</span></li>\n<li style=\"font-weight: 400;\" aria-level=\"1\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Which key performance indicators (KPIs) are most important to my business?</span></li>\n<li style=\"font-weight: 400;\" aria-level=\"1\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Which social media channels are we currently using?</span></li>\n</ul>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The answers to these questions will give you a solid foundation to build your influencer marketing strategy around. It’s far easier to get where you want to go if you know exactly where you are when you start your journey. It decreases your likelihood of getting lost along the way.</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">This set-up data is going to help you determine two of the most important parts of this SMASHing process: the supply chain influencers that are most in line with your business&#8217; niche and the creative direction you take to reach out to them.</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">#2. Manage</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The next step is to </span><b>manage the information</b><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> you gained through the set-up part of the process. Now that you have your foundational business data, what&#8217;s next? What’s next is making sure you can use that data to your benefit. You’ve determined where you’ve been, and now you need to know where you’re going next.</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">If the set-up portion of the SMASH process was gathering seeds, the manage portion is about planting them. Before you plant anything, you have to make sure the soil is fertile. Is </span><i><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">your</span></i><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> soil fertile? You can figure that out by asking yourself these questions:</span></p>\n<ul>\n<li style=\"font-weight: 400;\" aria-level=\"1\"><b>Are there any social media channels you’re not on that you should be using? </b><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">If so, it’s time to set up accounts. If you’re going to want to develop a successful influencer marketing strategy, you’re going to need the social presence required to reach out and build those key relationships.</span></li>\n<li style=\"font-weight: 400;\" aria-level=\"1\"><b>What resources do you have at your disposal?</b><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> In the introduction, I mentioned the two kinds of influencers are earned and paid ones. An earned influencer is one that promotes your product just because they like it. These require a lot of effort and nurturing, but come at less up front cost. Earned influencers can be volatile because you have no control over the narrative, but they&#8217;re still a possibility for any business that doesn&#8217;t have as much up front monetary budget. Otherwise, you have paid influencers, which are individuals you have offered compensation to in order to promote your product or service. </span></li>\n<li style=\"font-weight: 400;\" aria-level=\"1\"><b>What are your volume requirements?</b><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> If you’re interested in developing a SMASHing influencer marketing strategy, you’ll want to figure out how many influencers you’re interested in working with before moving forward. If you set a number too high, it’s easy to get overwhelmed, so start with a smaller, scalable number that can work and grow with you.</span></li>\n</ul>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Once you have these answers, it&#8217;ll become easier to create a plan for reaching out to and nurturing your influencers of choice. You have your analytical data and you&#8217;ve set up your social accounts and expectations, so the next step of your influencer marketing plan will be outreach. I&#8217;ve labeled this as the </span><b>answer</b><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> portion of the SMASH process because it answers the question of, &#8220;What do I need to do now to capture the interest of an influencer I want to work with?&#8221;</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">#3. Answer</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Here&#8217;s the part of the SMASH process that starts talking more directly about reaching out to influencers. There&#8217;s no influencer marketing without influencers, after all, and now we want to </span><a href=\"https://www.toprankblog.com/2021/04/hire-b2b-influencer-marketing-agency/\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"><b>answer questions</b></a> <span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">and develop a plan that accomplishes just that. The effort you&#8217;ve made in the last two steps should leave you feeling more than prepared for this part. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">To continue our gardening metaphor, if </span><b>set-up</b><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> was gathering seeds and </span><b>manage</b><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> was planting them, this portion of the process is laying down the fertilizer to make sure those seeds grow.</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">You’re going to start reaching out now, but before you do there are a couple more things to take care of first:</span></p>\n<ul>\n<li style=\"font-weight: 400;\" aria-level=\"1\"><b>Do you have analytics set-up for the social media channels you&#8217;re currently using?</b><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> If not, you&#8217;ll want that to be set up now so that the data can be utilized in the final step of this process. </span></li>\n<li style=\"font-weight: 400;\" aria-level=\"1\"><b>What are your brand standards and are they documented?</b><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> Influencer outreach is going to involve developing a successful online brand presence, and that will include having a modern and well developed look, tone, and general feel.</span></li>\n</ul>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">This is the step where you can start brainstorming and developing fun, creative content. Things like: </span></p>\n<ul>\n<li style=\"font-weight: 400;\" aria-level=\"1\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">A content plan for your website’s blog and social channels that focuses on the topics covered in set-up </span></li>\n<li style=\"font-weight: 400;\" aria-level=\"1\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">A plan for influencer outreach and a vetted list of the first influencers you want to reach out to</span></li>\n<li style=\"font-weight: 400;\" aria-level=\"1\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Steps you can take to capture influencer vision and make yourself a brand that your preferred influencers are going to want to work with</span></li>\n</ul>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The development of these types of detailed plans is almost always best left to a professional B2B marketing company. That doesn’t mean you can’t start on your own to gather ideas that fit with your already determined priorities and goals. </span></p>\n<p><b>One more important tip:</b><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> when you’re looking for a B2B marketing company to partner with to develop strategies like those listed in this part of the SMASH process, look for ones that self-label as </span><a href=\"https://www.toprankblog.com/2021/04/hire-b2b-influencer-marketing-agency/\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">influencer marketing experts</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">. If they prioritize influencer marketing enough to make it a part of their main service offering, they’ll have the sort of specialized expertise you’re going to want. </span></p>\n<ol start=\"4\">\n<li><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> Share</span></li>\n</ol>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Once you&#8217;re at the </span><b>share</b><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> portion of the SMASH process, stop to give yourself a pat on the back. You&#8217;ve already gone a long way toward significantly differentiating your supply chain business and should feel proud. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Of all the steps, this one is the most active. Unlike some of the others, the sharing portion will go on indefinitely because you&#8217;ll always be creating new content in need of promotion. During this part, you’re going to be focusing on getting the content you’ve started to create in front of the influencers you want to impress. You’ll be using the social media profiles that have been set up and gathering data about what’s working and what isn’t for analysis in the final part of the process. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Remember our gardening metaphor? Set-up is gathering seeds, manage is planting them, answer is fertilization, and share is making sure everything that has begun to sprout is properly watered.</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">It’s important to note that there is no one-size-fits-all approach to working with B2B influencers, especially in the supply chain industry. There will be unique factors to consider for each unique influencer company. That being said, here are a couple good rules of thumb to consider when attempting to engage influencers: </span></p>\n<ul>\n<li style=\"font-weight: 400;\" aria-level=\"1\"><b>Make them aware of you before you ask them for anything.</b><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> You want to give influencers a chance to be familiar with your brand before you reach out. This will make developing your partnership easier, because they&#8217;ll already have passive trust in your brand. This is also why it&#8217;s so important to have a </span><a href=\"https://www.toprankblog.com/2017/09/seo-research-tools-content/\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">content plan</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> before this point so that you’ve already laid the groundwork for better connections later on. </span></li>\n<li style=\"font-weight: 400;\" aria-level=\"1\"><b>Know what your goal is before reaching out. </b><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Influencers are busy people and aren&#8217;t going to want their time wasted. Don&#8217;t send out pitches or other contacts willy nilly. Instead, make sure you know your goal before initiating any sort of contact because that goal will influence the way you reach out. What do you want from this influencer? Are you interested in them sharing your content or attending an event? Providing a testimonial or creating a multi-part video series extolling the virtues of your product? Always plan before you preach.</span></li>\n</ul>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">You’re always going to partially be in the share stage as you work on your influencer marketing strategy. This is the part of the plan which focuses on connection and outreach, which is the cornerstone of influencer connections. The information you get from what works </span><i><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">and </span></i><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">what doesn’t work in this stage will help you in the next, final, one.</span></p>\n<ol start=\"4\">\n<li><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> Hypothesize</span></li>\n</ol>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">You&#8217;ve done most of the work and now you get to </span><b>hypothesize</b><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> about what comes next. This step is influenced by all the information and experience that has been gained from the four previous. You’ve planted and tended your garden and now you can see which crops are thriving and which need more help before a successful harvest.</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Remember when I told you it was important to set up analytics for all of your company social profiles? When you get to the </span><b>hypothesize</b><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> portion of the SMASH process, it&#8217;s time to look at that data and see what insight can be gleaned from it. Based on those insights, you can make tweaks and updates to your existing influencer marketing strategy to improve it&#8217;s overall success rate.</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">&#8211;</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Ask yourself: would I be more likely to invest in a product or service when it’s been recommended by someone I trust or admire? If your answer was yes, you’re not alone. That’s why influencer marketing has become a larger and more significant part of modern B2B marketing over time, and why the SMASH process was developed in the first place. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">If you’re interested in learning more about influencer marketing, you can find more information by </span><a href=\"https://www.toprankmarketing.com/influencer-marketing-supply-chain/\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">clicking here</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> and tuning into my appearance on the Let’s Talk Supply Chain podcast.</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">To everyone in the supply chain industry and beyond: I hope this process helps you find the same success it’s helped dozens of businesses before you achieve. Happy SMASHing!</span></p>\n<h3><strong>About The Author:</strong></h3>\n<p>As a proud founder and president of TopRank Marketing, Susan Misukanis helps B2B Technology companies achieve their full-funnel marketing goals.  She is relentlessly dedicated to helping brands move from chest-pounding self promotion to honest and meaningful conversations with their communities in a way that ultimately guides their buyer’s journeys.  On a daily basis, Susan works with her team to ceaselessly demonstrate TopRank values of truth, high-impact results and never ending learning!</p>\n",

    "uuid": "620d125c-6eec-4499-87f7-f3b49dee727e",
    "post_id": 4806,
    "type": "blogs",
    "title": "Collaboration meets visibility: Why FourKites recent funding success brings supply chain one step closer to the future",

    "web_content": "<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Everybody knows that there are two things I absolutely love: collaboration, and visibility. And never have these two things been more important than this past year. We’ve faced unprecedented times, as the COVID-19 pandemic tore through the industry, disrupting everything from manufacturing to shipping; whilst simultaneously demanding supply chain step up, as the safe movement of things like food, vaccines and essential household supplies became paramount. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">I’ve talked to so many businesses about the weaknesses the pandemic has exposed within our industry; the stress points its tested; the outdated methodologies and technologies it’s unveiled. But I’ve also talked a lot about the positives – the benefits that have come from shining a light on those hidden, or forgotten, weaknesses; the amazing agility and resilience we discovered (that we didn’t even know we had!); the new, more innovative mindsets that have emerged. And a renewed and enthusiastic commitment to collaboration and visibility are undeniably two of the most important outcomes. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">One company who’s really doubled down on their commitment to these two vital areas is </span><a href=\"https://www.fourkites.com/\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">FourKites</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">. Despite the struggles that much of the industry is still facing FourKites, a leading global supply chain software brand focused on bringing real-time visibility to supply chain, has incredibly just secured $100 million of Series D growth financing. This hugely important deal will help them to continue their mission of taking visibility end to end, connecting the physical and digital worlds of warehouses, stores and transportation with real-time data and machine learning to </span><a href=\"https://www.fourkites.com/future-of-digital-supply-chains/\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">transform supply chains</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> on an epic scale. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The investment comes courtesy of huge names THL, Volvo Group, Zebra Technologies, Qualcomm, August Capital, CEAS Investments, Hyde Park Angels, Hyde Park Venture Partners and Bain Capital – clearly demonstrating that FourKites isn&#8217;t the only big industry name committed to transforming global supply chain with end-to-end visibility, utilizing the power of collaboration. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Because these investors don’t just bring capital to the table; they aren’t just boastful, big business name drops. These partnerships are the definition of strategic alliance, where brand visions for customer satisfaction, technology, efficiency and everything in between truly align to create the most robust, innovative strategies to drive the industry forward. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Whilst THL shares a commitment to supply chain automation, Volvo Group Venture Capital focuses on trends that are shaping the future of transportation. Zebra Technologies brings leadership in enterprise asset intelligence and Qualcomm Ventures shares its scale and capabilities in wireless, 5G and IoT technologies. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">This supply chain supergroup brings fresh ideas, expertise, innovation and capabilities to the pioneering FourKites platform that will not only help to propel FourKites into the future, but will change the trajectory of the industry forever and set the tone for supply chain for years to come. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">FourKites has an amazing vision for the future, a vision that I share as well. A vision of interconnected, secure, intelligent networks where supply chain partners can find new ways to optimize operations, innovate and deliver greater customer service and value through real-time visibility.</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">And this new financing deal, combining capital with collaboration to deliver ultimate visibility, brings us all one step closer to that vision. </span></p>\n",

    "web_content": "<p><span data-contrast=\"auto\">If 2020 taught us anything, it’s to open our minds to new ideas.  New ways of working.  New ways of connecting.  New ways of marketing.  New ways of selling.  New ways of hiring.  </span><span data-contrast=\"auto\">And n</span><span data-contrast=\"auto\">ew ways of growing.  Disruption </span><span data-contrast=\"auto\">has a way of doing</span><span data-contrast=\"auto\"> that, and the nimblest </span><span data-contrast=\"auto\">organizations</span><span data-contrast=\"auto\"> </span><span data-contrast=\"auto\">are </span><span data-contrast=\"auto\">able to pivot in changing environments </span><span data-contrast=\"auto\">and</span><span data-contrast=\"auto\"> win. </span><span data-ccp-props=\"{}\"> </span></p>\n<p><span data-contrast=\"auto\">In the midst of a global pandemic w</span><span data-contrast=\"auto\">ith remote work becoming </span><span data-contrast=\"auto\">not just preferred but, in many cases, </span><span data-contrast=\"auto\">mandatory, virtual workspaces and work-from-home situations quickly switched from </span><span data-contrast=\"auto\">a</span><span data-contrast=\"auto\"> business owner’</span><span data-contrast=\"auto\">s</span><span data-contrast=\"auto\"> biggest fear to </span><span data-contrast=\"auto\">a proven model of productivity and efficiency</span><span data-contrast=\"auto\">.  This change in perspective created</span><span data-contrast=\"auto\"> </span><span data-contrast=\"auto\">an opportunity to </span><span data-contrast=\"auto\">save money and hire the best talent regardless of where </span><span data-contrast=\"auto\">a </span><span data-contrast=\"auto\">prospective employee resided, whether within or outside of the United States.  </span><span data-ccp-props=\"{}\"> </span></p>\n<p><span data-contrast=\"auto\">This transition opened up new possibilities for logistics companies across North America to reconsider their strategy </span><span data-contrast=\"auto\">for</span><span data-contrast=\"auto\"> scaling their business</span><span data-contrast=\"auto\">es</span><span data-contrast=\"auto\"> in a post-COVID world, which is why <a href=\"https://leanstaffing.com/\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\">Lean Solutions Group</a> continue</span><span data-contrast=\"auto\">d</span><span data-contrast=\"auto\"> to grow.  For the past eight years, we have supported our clients with an incredible pool of bilingual, highly talented and highly motivated professionals from one of five </span><span data-contrast=\"auto\">amazing </span><span data-contrast=\"auto\">cities in Colombia</span><span data-contrast=\"auto\"> with our innovative nearshore staffing model.  In an unpredictable year like 2020, Lean </span><span data-contrast=\"auto\">grew to </span><span data-contrast=\"auto\">over 2,000 employees, all of which are successfully working from home</span><span data-contrast=\"auto\">, although we can’t wait to get back to the office to show off the energy and culture within our amazing facilities.</span><span data-contrast=\"auto\">  </span><span data-ccp-props=\"{}\"> </span></p>\n<p><span data-contrast=\"auto\">The nearshore staffing model is named after the fact that most Colombians understand the American culture, speak great English and are excited to work with North American countries</span><span data-contrast=\"auto\">, even though they are a couple thousand miles offshore</span><span data-contrast=\"auto\">.  Many of our team members spent time in the states as kids or went to college </span><span data-contrast=\"auto\">in an English-speaking country, improving their speaking &amp; writing skills, and understanding the American culture of sports &amp; entertainment.  </span><span data-ccp-props=\"{}\"> </span></p>\n<p><span data-contrast=\"auto\">As a result, this partnership business</span><span data-contrast=\"auto\"> model takes the best aspects of traditional outsourcing</span><span data-contrast=\"auto\">, </span><span data-contrast=\"auto\">but </span><span data-contrast=\"auto\">wit</span><span data-contrast=\"auto\">h more management control and the highest levels of IT security</span><span data-contrast=\"auto\">.  Best of all, </span><span data-contrast=\"auto\">it’s </span><span data-contrast=\"auto\">significantly </span><span data-contrast=\"auto\">easier </span><span data-contrast=\"auto\">to establish this model </span><span data-contrast=\"auto\">than </span><span data-contrast=\"auto\">it is to </span><span &amp; logistics industry, working with over 150 clients, including 9 publicly traded companies, all of our employees are highly trained in transportation &amp; logistics.  </span><span data-ccp-props=\"{}\"> </span></p>\n<p><span data-contrast=\"auto\">The Lean story began some 25 years ago with our Founder and CEO, Robert Cadena, who grew up on the northern shore of Colombia in the quaint, tourist city of Cartagena.  In coming to the states for college, he began his transportation career working on a loading dock and eventually started his own LTL brokerage.  In an effort to maximize his margins and bring economic opportunity to his hometown, he set up his back office operations in Cartagena, training his team to handle the myriad of issues that arise in logistics.  </span><span data-ccp-props=\"{}\"> </span></p>\n<p><span data-contrast=\"auto\">In time, his company was acquired by a larger broker looking for an LTL offering, and in doing its due diligence, recognized the value of having back office operations in Colombia with professional employees providing quality customer service.  That’s when the light bulb went off and Robert realized this model would be valuable to other brokerages as well.  </span><span data-ccp-props=\"{}\"> </span></p>\n<p><span data-contrast=\"auto\">In partnering with David Bell, Lean Solutions Group was </span><span data-contrast=\"auto\">formed  in</span><span data-contrast=\"auto\"> 2012, and the nearshoring model began to gain traction among logistics companies, including some of the largest freight brokerages and 3PLs in the industry.</span><span data-contrast=\"auto\"> </span><span data-contrast=\"auto\"> </span><span data-contrast=\"auto\">In the past two years, the focus has shifted to include new offerings based on customer requests, including IT developers and tech-based projects through Lean Tech.  In 2020, Lean began offering sales &amp; marketing support through Lean Sales and Lean Marketing, with customers recognizing the value of building a partnership with a company that truly understand every aspect of their business.   </span><span data-ccp-props=\"{}\"> </span></p>\n<h3><strong>About The Author:</strong></h3>\n<p><img decoding=\"async\" class=\"alignleft wp-image-4597 size-thumbnail\"     "web_content": "<p>The strangest and most complicated year of this century is over, we are now in 2021, called the year of hope &#8230;. in the form of vaccines and cure for this damn virus that has infected more than 80MM of people, and killed already almost 2MM globally. We will all wish to return to the world we lived in before Covid19 arrival.</p>\n<p>From 2020 to 2021 in theory only 1 digit changes, but this single number feeds millions of dreams and wishes made by all citizens of our planet, after several hard months of restrictions, suffering limitations on what was once our &#8220;normal&#8221; life.</p>\n<p>We have been many months without traveling, going out to restaurants, enjoying with our friends, hug each other naturally and now we even need to wear a protective mask to walk in the street in several countries. Many governments have restricted our temporal or geographical freedom of movement.</p>\n<p>If we think about it for a moment, we will see that we´ve made all these great sacrifices to stop the virus, because no one wants to sacrifice their individual rights at any time and wants to continue to maintain them, whatever the existing external threat.</p>\n<p>Now it is a question of gaining the right to end this long period of restrictions, reducing the virus capacity to infect others, probably assuming some permanent changes in our global life dynamics. These new rules are yet to be determined, because no one knows for sure which of the transformations experienced will end up being permanent for all.</p>\n<p>One initial recommended new routine action that we can do is to extreme the quality of our food, ensuring our immune system is as well prepared as possible to defend itself with more guarantee from the virus infection.</p>\n<p>I would now like to share the summary of my learnings from 2020 just finished, and provide some tips for 2021, which I will implement in order to improve my existence and that of those around me, as far as possible.</p>\n<h2>My five main learnings for 2020 have been:</h2>\n<p>* We all need freedom: When we lack it, we value it much more. We must never lose it, and, in any case, have the inner strength to find it at all times, despite any external physical constraints. At least, we always have the freedom of our minds!</p>\n<p>* Personal development requires that we know ourselves, especially how to recognize and manage our own emotions. If you can notice them in advance, much better!</p>\n<p>* Global changes and transformations are not (only) linked to technology, but depend on our ability to understand and manage them satisfactorily.</p>\n<p>* Open transparent communications are key for people to understand each other</p>\n<p>* The &#8220;Supply Chain&#8221; (as an integration of all operations &amp; logistics process functions) has been consolidated as a critical area of ​​business, in all sectors of activity.</p>\n<h2>As for my tips for this 2021, with more personal and professional growth, they are:</h2>\n<p>1.- Open your mind, like an umbrella, and allow yourself CHANGES AND TRANSFORMATIONS: Train your curiosity, be creative and innovative and avoid saying &#8220;NO&#8221; as first answer to any change proposal.</p>\n<p>2.- Allow yourself personal development moments on a regular basis: Some people may think they do not need help, but an accompaniment to overcome our most difficult challenges is always a lever to get out more easily and perform better in less time.</p>\n<p>3.- Communicate, collaborate and coordinate with everyone else: We can be alone in many moments, but to advance in personal and/or professional projects it will always be necessary to do so by interacting with several people. Knowing how to do it right will be key to success.</p>\n<p>4.- Use professional networking as a lever to develop: No one ever has all the answers, but there are people who are so well connected that they always know who to ask their unsolved questions.</p>\n<p>5.- Talent development must always have time allocated in your agenda, either for yourself and for your teams.</p>\n<p>Finally, I wish you all a year full of happiness, personal and professional successes and improvements, in a world full of health and economic recovery for all humans.</p>\n<p>Let&#8217;s take care of ourselves &amp; continue transforming.</p>\n<h3><strong>About The Author:</strong></h3>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.linkedin.com/in/miquelserracanta/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer nofollow\">Miquel Serracanta</a> is a business advisor, focused on Supply Chain, by serving the global supply chain community in optimizing End-to-End Supply Chains. Our services include Organization, Talent development (Head-hunting, Trainings, Kaizen events, Workshops, Team activities), Strategy design &amp; implementation, Planning (S&amp;OP, IBP) Projects &amp; Processes continuous improvement and all SC functions performance improvement in a synchronized way: Procurement, Logistics, Transportation, Warehousing, Distribution, Last Mile, Customer Service.</p>\n<p>&nbsp;</p>\n",

  {
    "uuid": "4f74d716-77ae-4540-a949-09367cc91fc8",
    "post_id": 4376,
    "type": "blogs",
    "title": "Putting the Smart in Smarter Logistics",
    "slug": "putting-the-smart-in-smarter-logistics",
    "date": "2020-12-10T08:00:46",
    "summary": null,
    "main_points": null,
    "recent_news": null,
    "related_articles": [],
    "web_content": "<p>It is not a secret that technology evolves at an accelerated rate.  As an example, I have seen the progress of vinyl records to cassettes to compact discs to playable digital files and finally to streaming media.  My teenage sons, on the other hand, have never owned a CD and barely recall downloading mp3s.</p>\n<p>One of the more interesting advances in technology, particularly in a business and consumer setting is in the area of Artificial Intelligence (AI) and Machine Learning (ML).  Building upon the confluence of device (sensor) proliferation, high speed data ingestion and advances in computing power, AI/ML produces use case-driven insights that we leverage in what seems like all aspects of our lives.</p>\n<p>It is an advancing space that is both obvious &#8211; think of the personal assistant on the smart phone of your choice &#8211; and yet subtle – think of the fitness device insights and streaming service viewing suggestions &#8211; at the same time.</p>\n<p>In the world of logistics, the contributing forces are similar.  The availability of disparate data and highly scalable ingestion engines, the advent of performant and elastic public clouds, and the wider adoption of open application program interfaces (APIs), presents a ripe opportunity to apply AI/ML to provide unique, incremental value.</p>\n<p>But like many things, how do you separate hype from reality?  In our consumer world, if our streaming service suggests something that we wouldn’t watch, we just skip over it.  If my fitness watch tells me to rest when my coach tells me to train, then I train.  In the world of supply chain, however, poor or weak insights have real impact and real cost.</p>\n<p>To separate the wheat from the chaff, I suggest considering three approaches:</p>\n<ol>\n<li><strong>Avoid the general:</strong> Many solutions will boast being “AI/ML powered” as if it is just something you turn on and it magically makes things better but that is not how it works. Learning models are designed to focus on specific cases.  Labor and order forecasting, and transportation risk assessments are good examples of particular use cases.</li>\n<li><strong>The right data in abundance:</strong> AI/ML models require data and lots of it. The good news is that in today’s age, data is abundant.  The more difficult question is understanding what data the model is trained to ingest and leverage and how reliable are those data sources.  A model to evaluate execution risk on planned loads will be limited if the scope and availability of constraint and network data are overly simple or unreliable.</li>\n<li><strong>Proven in reality: </strong>It is easy to come up with a premise of value, but a premise is immaterial unless it is tested with real data ingestion and measured against a control. Only by creating real world circumstances can a premise be proven and more importantly measured.</li>\n</ol>\n<p>Applying this in practice, let’s take an example of a logistics solution promising AI/ML powered routing.  Working through the steps:</p>\n<ol>\n<li><strong>Avoid the general:</strong> What aspect of route planning is being improved? e.g. load fill rate, driver assignment, route sequence.</li>\n<li><strong>The right data in abundance:</strong> What data is the model leveraging? What is the timeliness and reliability of that data? What is the scope of the data being considered?</li>\n<li><strong>Proven in reality: </strong>Has the problem been solved in a real-world scenario? In what circumstances e.g. a grocery environment will have different data and considerations than an industrial manufacturer.</li>\n</ol>\n<p>The acceleration of technology is enough to give anyone pause.  The opportunity these advancements present are unprecedented but also forces us to really understand what data is there.  By interrogating three simple perspectives, we can quickly separate the real from the noise and take our logistics networks from vinyl to streaming.</p>\n<h2>About the Author</h2>\n<p><strong>Fabrizio Brasca, Group Vice President, Global Solutions, Blue Yonder</strong></p>\n<p><img fetchpriority=\"high\" decoding=\"async\" class=\"alignleft size-medium wp-image-4379\" src=\"https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/Fab-Brasca-Headshot-2020-200x300.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"200\" height=\"300\" title=\"\" srcset=\"https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/Fab-Brasca-Headshot-2020-200x300.jpg 200w, https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/Fab-Brasca-Headshot-2020-600x900.jpg 600w, https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/Fab-Brasca-Headshot-2020-683x1024.jpg 683w, https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/Fab-Brasca-Headshot-2020-768x1152.jpg 768w, https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/Fab-Brasca-Headshot-2020.jpg 1000w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 200px) 100vw, 200px\" />Fabrizio (Fab) Brasca is group vice president (GVP), global solutions at Blue Yonder.  In this role, he leads his organization to drive thought leadership, go-to-market strategy and solution execution excellence for Blue Yonder’s 4,000+ customer base.  Additionally, his organization works closely with customers to understand requirements, drive best practices and adoption of Blue Yonder solutions across the globe.</p>\n<p>Previously, he was VP of solution strategy, supply chain execution, responsible for developing innovative strategies across all industry verticals, strengthening executive-level relationships with JDA’s key customers and prospects and advising companies on best practices to become more profitable. Fab joined Blue Yonder as part of the i2 Technologies acquisition in January 2010 after spending more than 10 years at i2 serving in transportation-focused senior management positions. In these roles, he helped lead i2’s global transportation practice including marketing, presales, roadmap development and services functions.</p>\n<p>He holds an Honours Bachelor of Mathematics, with a specialization in business and information systems from the University of Waterloo in Canada.</p>\n",

  {
    "uuid": "bff39942-75e4-46ea-9da3-d6e83deb39e9",
    "post_id": 4361,
    "type": "blogs",
    "title": "What your freight broker isn’t telling you about quality and compliance",
    "slug": "what-your-freight-broker-isnt-telling-you-about-quality-and-compliance",
    "date": "2020-12-08T08:00:17",
    "summary": null,
    "main_points": null,
    "recent_news": null,
    "related_articles": [],
    "web_content": "<p>With volume spikes, prolonged truck price increases, and record-level tender rejections, 2020 has been one of the most volatile years in recent freight market history. If you’re like most shippers we’ve talked to, you’ve had to work hard this year to get the coverage you need, and have brought on new capacity providers to fill the gap. Are you taking into consideration all of the quality and compliance risks of your providers?</p>\n<p>The drivers who move your product present legal, financial, service and reputational risks for your business. Read on to learn why quality and compliance is something you should be talking about with your brokers and carriers, what questions you should be asking, and how Machine Learning is being used to change the game when it comes to driver quality and compliance.</p>\n<h2>The risks of quality and compliance in freight</h2>\n<p>At a high level, shippers face legal, financial, service and reputation risks every time they ship freight.</p>\n<p><img fetchpriority=\"high\" decoding=\"async\" class=\"aligncenter wp-image-4363 size-full\" src=\"https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/convoy-.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"977\" height=\"454\" title=\"\" srcset=\"https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/convoy-.png 977w, https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/convoy--600x279.png 600w, https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/convoy--300x139.png 300w, https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/convoy--768x357.png 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 977px) 100vw, 977px\" /></p>\n<p><b>Legal risks &#8211;</b> On the legal side, there has been a trend over the past 10-15 years where shippers can be held liable for the actions of their carriers via vicarious liability. Similarly, a precedent has been set around negligent hiring. Here, if the carrier hauling the load is deemed unfit (due to authority, insurance, safety history, or some other reason) legal ramifications can come down on the shipper.</p>\n<p><b>Financial risks &#8211; </b>Not only are there the legal costs if you are pulled into a lawsuit but also compensatory costs if you are held liable, as well as increased insurance costs. Plus, poor-quality drivers lead to a higher number of cargo claims which can have a material impact on transportation costs.</p>\n<p><b>Service and reputation risks &#8211; </b>Service and reputation often go hand in hand. Poor service such as late pickups and deliveries, accidents, and cargo damage can have negative implications for the service you give to your customers and your ability to continue to earn their business</p>\n<h2>The pitfalls of using CSA ratings for quality and compliance</h2>\n<p>Many traditional brokers and asset carriers who broker loads use the FMCSA’s CSA ratings to determine whether or not a driver is good to haul. This approach has a lot of blind-spots because the CSA rating program was not meant to be used as a mechanism to understand carrier safety and compliance. In fact, it was designed solely for enforcement authorities to intervene with very poor performing carriers.</p>\n<p>Based on time and resources, the FMCSA only does a full inspection of carriers who have been flagged by their system. Typically, only carriers with a significant amount of safety violations qualify for a full review which means that a startling 95% of carriers are not rated at all.</p>\n<p><img decoding=\"async\" class=\"aligncenter wp-image-4364 size-full\" src=\"https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/convoy-2.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"977\" height=\"495\" title=\"\" srcset=\"https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/convoy-2.png 977w, https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/convoy-2-600x304.png 600w, https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/convoy-2-300x152.png 300w, https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/convoy-2-768x389.png 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 977px) 100vw, 977px\" /></p>\n<p>&nbsp;</p>\n<p>When capacity providers rely on CSA ratings to vet their drivers they have very limited visibility into the vast majority of safety records. This prevents an adequate assessment of carrier and driver safety during hiring and leads to a lot of uncertainty for shippers.</p>\n<h2>Five questions you should be asking to improve quality and reduce risk</h2>\n<p>Not sure where to start? Use these five questions to check-in with your brokers and carriers to make sure you’re on the same page.</p>\n<ol>\n<li><strong>Are you registered, licensed and bonded? </strong>This may seem basic, and it is. But if you or your team is frantically trying to find coverage for backup or spot, this fundamental step can be overlooked, and introduce significant risk.</li>\n</ol>\n<ol start=\"2\">\n<li><strong>What types of insurance do you have, and what do you require of your carriers?  </strong>A freight partner with a comprehensive and thoughtfully designed suite of insurance policies will be a better partner in managing risk. sleep easier at night by verifying that your freight partner has  the following core types of coverage or suitable equivalents: Broker liability, excess liability, contingent and additional transportation cargo coverage, workers compensation and employer liability, crime, and mandatory broker bond insurance.</li>\n</ol>\n<ol start=\"3\">\n<li><strong>How is carrier and driver safety assessed?  </strong>Accidents are an unfortunate reality in this industry, so you need to take proactive steps to mitigate risk by requiring transportation partners to set safety standards that are acceptable for your business. Ask for a list of what their safety standards are. You should be provided with a speedy and thorough reply that amounts to more than “We don’t use unsatisfactory rated carriers.”</li>\n</ol>\n<ol start=\"4\">\n<li><strong>How often are carriers screened and audited after onboarding?  </strong>It’s not enough to check for compliance requirements at the time of onboarding. Even regularly scheduled static checks (e.g. once a quarter or, gasp, once a year) of carriers is insufficient. We recommend working with partners who can audit their carriers automatically and in real time — at least daily if not more frequently.</li>\n</ol>\n<ol start=\"5\">\n<li><strong>How do you identify and address fraud?  </strong>In this industry, data is a powerful tool that everyone should use to prevent fraud. Your transportation providers should have a clear process to identify fraudulent sign-ups onto their platform.</li>\n</ol>\n<h2>How Machine Learning is changing the quality and compliance landscape</h2>\n<p>At Convoy, in order to safely and accurately vet our carrier network we created a robust <a href=\"https://convoy.com/shippers/quality-safety-compliance/\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\">quality and compliance program</a> from the ground-up. This industry-leading program leverages a rich data set and vet carriers not just once, but every single time they are assigned to a load. This is where Machine Learning comes in.</p>\n<p>There are thousands of data inputs, like speeding violations and inspection outcomes, that can be vetted across millions of carrier records, which means information is changing all the time. Not only is identifying the safest carriers a challenge, but being able to constantly monitor compliance as it fluctuates in real-time is a feat no human can accomplish. Convoy uses Machine Learning to process millions of inputs in a short time, correlate them to crash likelihood, and generate a score for every carrier that indicates how safe that carrier actually is.</p>\n<p>The more data we feed our model, the more accurate it becomes, and because it’s a learning algorithm, it actually gets better over time, driving incremental accuracy and better results. This approach has resulted in a carrier network with 16% fewer accidents compared to the rest of the industry, as well as a claims-incident ratio that is 20x lower than the industry average. With Machine Learning, Convoy has taken the guesswork out of carrier safety assessment, and replaced it with concrete, data-based modeling to yield bottom-line results for our shippers.</p>\n<p><img decoding=\"async\" class=\"aligncenter wp-image-4365 size-full\" src=\"https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/convoy-3.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"977\" height=\"487\" title=\"\" srcset=\"https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/convoy-3.png 977w, https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/convoy-3-600x299.png 600w, https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/convoy-3-300x150.png 300w, https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/convoy-3-768x383.png 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 977px) 100vw, 977px\" /></p>\n<p><a href=\"https://convoy.com/bookatruck\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"><em>Sign up</em></a><em> for Convoy’s free shipper platform today and start taking advantage of the benefits of Convoy’s industry-leading quality and compliance approach. Or, tune in to Let’s Talk Supply Chain on Tuesday, December 15th to hear Lorin Seeks, Director of Quality and Compliance at Convoy, dive deeper into this topic with a special focus on small and midsize businesses. </em></p>\n<h2>About Convoy</h2>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" decoding=\"async\" class=\"alignleft wp-image-4369 size-thumbnail\" src=\"https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/C_block_roarange-Sabrina-Kautz-150x150.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"150\" height=\"150\" title=\"\" srcset=\"https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/C_block_roarange-Sabrina-Kautz-150x150.png 150w, https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/C_block_roarange-Sabrina-Kautz-300x300.png 300w, https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/C_block_roarange-Sabrina-Kautz-100x100.png 100w, https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/C_block_roarange-Sabrina-Kautz-600x600.png 600w, https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/C_block_roarange-Sabrina-Kautz-1024x1024.png 1024w, https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/C_block_roarange-Sabrina-Kautz-768x768.png 768w, https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/C_block_roarange-Sabrina-Kautz-1536x1536.png 1536w, https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/C_block_roarange-Sabrina-Kautz-2048x2048.png 2048w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 150px) 100vw, 150px\" /><a href=\"https://convoy.com/\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\">Convoy</a> is the nation’s most efficient digital freight network. We move thousands of truckloads throughout the U.S. and cross-border to Canada through our optimized, connected network of carriers, saving money for shippers, increasing earnings for drivers, and eliminating carbon waste for our planet. We use technology and data to solve problems of waste and inefficiency in the $800B trucking industry, which generates over 72 million metric tons of wasted CO2 emissions from empty trucks. Fortune 500 shippers like Anheuser-Busch, P&amp;G, Niagara, and Unilever trust Convoy to lower costs, increase logistics efficiency, and achieve environmental sustainability targets.</p>\n",

    "title": "Conquering COVID-19",
    "slug": "conquering-covid-19",

    "web_content": "<p><span style=\"color: #333333; font-size: 26px;\">An Assault Plan for COVID-19 Vaccine Supply Chain Distribution</span></p>\n<div class=\"wpb_text_column wpb_content_element \">\n<div class=\"wpb_wrapper\">\n<p>The impact of the COVID-19 pandemic is of global significance, and 2020 is not a year that will soon be forgotten. The development of COVID-19 vaccines are imminent and seen as a solution that the world is looking for to see a return to some semblance of normal. When vaccines are available, getting the vaccine from production to the global population will be the next challenge.</p>\n<p>Vaccine development is the first step in an extensive distribution process. Governments need to plan and build the strategies, infrastructure, and organization to manage the post-production supply chain for vaccine delivery. There will be significant differences between the global north and the global south in how governments can address these challenges.</p>\n<p>A vaccine delivery ecosystem is required to coordinate this supply chain challenge. This VDE is a public-private partnership (PPP) that orchestrates the private and public networks to ensure that populations are effectively inoculated. This blueprint provides an overview that includes problem definition, direction, and opportunities for technology use cases in addressing:</p>\n<ul>\n<li>The global distribution process’s scale and complexity, requiring processes, checks, and balances that provide supply chain control.</li>\n<li>The integrity and security of the vaccine, along with the protection of the information that goes with it. This protection level needs to occur through storage, delivery, and transport of the cargo as it travels within and between countries.</li>\n<li>Customs and international border crossing procedures, which need to be reviewed to prevent disruptions and delays, destroying the vaccine through poor temperature control, mishandling or incorrect documentation.</li>\n<li>End-to-end monitoring of temperature, ensuring the integrity of documents and data to meet compliance requirements, and last-mile distribution all need to be assured to reduce waste and slow the pace of the virus.</li>\n<li>The integration with healthcare systems to meet further compliance requirements and coordinate with any ad-hoc or interim facilities or procedures that may be required.</li>\n<li>The complexity of workforce, patient, PPE, and inventory scheduling.</li>\n</ul>\n<p>This blueprint developed by the Logistics &amp; Supply Chain Management Society (LSCMS) in collaboration with <a href=\"https://www.idc.com/\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\">IDC</a>, serves as an awareness tool to drive open engagement between stakeholders to discuss safe and effective options for ensuring vaccination distribution with minimal waste and maximum integrity to the world’s population.</p>\n<h2></h2>\n<h2 style=\"text-align: center;\"><a href=\"https://logisym.org/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/LSCMS-IDC-Conquering-COVID19-supply-chain-vaccine-v1-final.pdf\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" target=\"_blank\"><strong>Download the full report here.</strong></a></h2>\n</div>\n</div>\n<h2><strong>About LogiSYM</strong></h2>\n<p>LogiSYM is the collaborative platform of The Logistics &amp; Supply Chain Management Society and engages the industry through its collaborative platforms, LogiSYM and CargoNOW.</p>\n<p>Practically all areas of the Logistics spectrum are represented and connected. Shippers, Freight Forwarders, Academics, Students, Carriers, Personal Effects Movers and other individuals and organisations form the core of our network of more than 100,000 Logisticians.</p>\n<p>With an emphasis on commercial experience and expertise LogiSYM is the leading community for the development of Logistics in the region and work with our members, government, organisations and professionals in raising the profile and expertise through a range of activities.</p>\n<p>LogiSYM has the proven history, framework, value for money and strategic reach to make it the right choice for you.</p>\n<ul>\n<li>To promote professional development of Logistics and Supply Chain Management;</li>\n<li>To serve as a resource centre for parties interested in Logistics and Supply Chain Management</li>\n</ul>\n<h2><strong>The Authors:</strong></h2>\n<p><img decoding=\"async\" class=\"wp-image-4308 size-thumbnail alignleft\" src=\"https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/DSC4545-raymon-corporate-copy-150x150.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"150\" height=\"150\" title=\"\" srcset=\"https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/DSC4545-raymon-corporate-copy-150x150.jpg 150w, https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/DSC4545-raymon-corporate-copy-300x300.jpg 300w, https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/DSC4545-raymon-corporate-copy-100x100.jpg 100w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 150px) 100vw, 150px\" /></p>\n<p>&nbsp;</p>\n<p>&nbsp;</p>\n<p>&nbsp;</p>\n<p>Dr. Raymon Krishnan</p>\n<p>President, The Logistics &amp;   {
    "uuid": "d5bf2df5-5eda-4ebc-83cd-e1a1f2aafae2",
    "post_id": 4097,
    "type": "blogs",
    "title": "It&#8217;s Hard to Understate the Importance of TCO",
    "slug": "its-hard-to-understate-the-importance-of-tco",
    "date": "2020-11-03T08:00:32",
    "summary": null,
    "main_points": null,
    "recent_news": null,
    "related_articles": [],
    "web_content": "<p>One of the most important people in your company may not even be in the room when you make big procurement decisions. If you choose a supplier and don’t have a supply chain manager in the conversation, you run the risk of taking on a contract that will leave you wanting.</p>\n<p>Too often, supply chains are afterthoughts, and initial costs are the focus of procurement. However, the “per piece price” mindset covers only a fraction of the total cost of ownership (TCO) over the full life of an item. Remaining aware of TCO can help organizations make every budgeted dollar go further.</p>\n<h2>The benefits are often ongoing</h2>\n<p>Simply stated, the TCO approach asks you to consider your entire business and not just single costs. Then the equation can shift from saving money on a part or tool’s initial cost to developing cost savings that can be realized on a reoccurring basis.</p>\n<p>With a mix of hard and soft cost savings, TCO’s benefits come in the form of freed-up time and additional production from existing resources.</p>\n<p>TCO solutions are aimed at chipping away at the total cost of ownership. The goal is to find a way to do more with less: to manage inventory more effectively, to streamline processes, and to eliminate waste.</p>\n<p>This is particularly important when it comes to MRO, where piece price can typically represent less than 50% of the total costs associated with low-dollar, high-use supplies. (Think of safety goggles or earplugs.) And while commodity pricing is a key element, an even greater savings opportunity can often be found in the many indirect costs associated with acquiring, owning, and managing inventory. Some strategic TCO partners in the market today will assume that work and those costs – thus alleviating you and freeing up savings that can be reinvested in growth-driving areas of the business.</p>\n<h2>AREAS TO CONSIDER</h2>\n<p>Nothing has a single cost. Think of these factors to help develop a TCO mindset.</p>\n<ul>\n<li><strong>Purchase Price:</strong> The price paid</li>\n<li><strong>Acquisition Cost:</strong> Time spent to research, order, receive, inventory, and disperse an item.</li>\n<li><strong>Freight:</strong> Shipping and handling</li>\n<li><strong>Operation:</strong> The cost of using an item, i.e. fuel or electricity</li>\n<li><strong>Maintenance:</strong> Any costs associated with maintaining, repairing, and servicing</li>\n<li><strong>Lifespan:</strong> How long an item will last before it needs replacing</li>\n<li><strong>Additional Costs:</strong> Financing, any disposal fees, and insurance or warranty</li>\n</ul>\n<h2>Every Step Should Add Value</h2>\n<p>If there are steps in your workflows that do not add value to your end-user, how can you reduce or eliminate those steps? Quality Assurance adds value because it ensures defects aren’t reaching customers. How does stocking parts add value? Often, it doesn’t.</p>\n<p>Finding a third party to handle that work means your employees have more time to do what they do best: create your product, serve your customers, and grow your business.</p>\n<p>Partnering with an expert can go a long way toward reaping TCO benefits. They can help you standardize what’s included in your TCO planning, set how results are measured, and regularly review how things are going. <em>A truly strategic partner will share usage data with you to provide visibility so you can adapt and grow your business. </em></p>\n<h2>The Big Takeaway</h2>\n<p>There’s more to a purchase than the initial payment, and a TCO attitude can keep benefiting the bottom line. Even if a supply chain manager isn’t in the room with you for some conversations, that TCO mindset can be.</p>\n<p><img fetchpriority=\"high\" decoding=\"async\" class=\"alignnone size-medium wp-image-4138\" src=\"https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Picture1-300x188.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"300\" height=\"188\" title=\"\" srcset=\"https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Picture1-300x188.png 300w, https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Picture1.png 380w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 300px) 100vw, 300px\" /> <img decoding=\"async\" class=\"alignnone size-medium wp-image-4139\" src=\"https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Picture2-300x233.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"300\" height=\"233\" title=\"\" srcset=\"https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Picture2-300x233.png 300w, https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Picture2.png 341w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 300px) 100vw, 300px\" /></p>\n<h2><strong>About The Author:</strong></h2>\n<p><img decoding=\"async\" class=\"wp-image-4148 size-thumbnail alignleft\" src=\"https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Nathan-150x150.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"150\" height=\"150\" title=\"\" srcset=\"https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Nathan-150x150.jpg 150w, https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Nathan-300x300.jpg 300w, https://letstalksupplychain.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Nathan-100x100.jpg 100w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 150px) 100vw, 150px\" />Besides TCO, <a href=\"https://www.linkedin.com/in/nathan-hassler-4ab41b194/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer nofollow\">Nathan Hassler</a> also helps customers with supply chain solutions like Lean manufacturing, point-of-use inventory, and strategic partnerships. And as part of the team at Fastenal, Nathan is always working to help procurement professionals find new ways to become more productive.</p>\n",

    "uuid": "9f346bb3-62a8-43fd-878d-13b2aeaf34a8",
    "post_id": 3894,
    "type": "blogs",
    "title": "Supply Chain Talent: The Treasure to Find &#038; Keep",
    "slug": "supply-chain-talent-the-treasure-to-find-keep",
    "date": "2020-09-22T08:00:19",
    "summary": null,
    "main_points": null,
    "recent_news": null,
    "related_articles": [],
    "web_content": "<p>The most common consumer behavior during sales periods is bargain article search, especially articles with high value but significantly lower price than regular. This happen in all markets, including stock exchange. But there are always other people willing to get rid of some assets, believing in the opposite criteria: stocks are worth less than current market prices, so they want to recover their money sooner, before losing more in that downward trend. So, the real value of an article, product or stock is a subjective criteria, based on individual needs, analysis &amp; interpretation of future market evolution.</p>\n<p>The issue here appears when an item that was bought for a very low price -cheaper than others- performs poorly in quality and/or requirements compared with what was expected initially by its buyer. This issue will make him/her buy a new substitute item, generating a higher total cost of the item compared with what they would have paid if they bought the more expensive one initially, with likely higher quality &amp; performance.</p>\n<p>I would now like to link this to talent management and professional career development, in which we are suffering an era of constant bargains and salary reductions. Taking advantage of the excess of professionals actively job searching in the face of a lower demand for candidates by companies, when they hire staff they are lowering the salary proposals they offer in order to save money. When the number of available professionals in the market exceeds the number of positions to fill there, like it has been happening in last 5/6 years in some developed countries (ie: Spain), salaries for equivalent positions are reduced by 20-30% at different organizational levels, a trend driven by the search for short-term financial savings.</p>\n<p>By this practice, each of the hiring companies enter a negative spiral towards less talent retainment and additional loss of talent, which try to move themselves to healthier business environments. This business negative circle continues when these low performing companies choose to hire less prepared candidates -then paying less money to them-, achieving short-term financial savings, but failing to capture enough talent to make their business high performing and thus sustainable over time.</p>\n<p>On the other side, companies that have not entered into such short-term dynamic of solely focusing on economic cost reductions, have been able to better retain their talent and attract new additional talent, which certainly gives them a medium/long term greater value, thanks to the contributions that this greater human capital will provide their businesses, for sure. In short, saving on talent is, in my opinion, a huge mistake, although in the short term it can mean immediate savings, in the medium term would lead the company to a much worse scenario than the original, with poorer business results. So, a professional who really has a value is worth it, and should be paid accordingly and fairly based on its contributions in the short, medium and long term, without rebates or salary reductions. Achieving savings by hiring at a price lower than the real market value can never be considered a good practice by a headhunter company or a hiring company. Warren Buffet once said: &#8220;Hire the best and let them do what they know, instead of hiring the cheapest to do what you tell them to&#8221;, obviously the results will be very different in both cases.</p>\n<p>I&#8217;m sure that today hiring companies don&#8217;t select candidates who do not initially meet the required technical (&#8220;hard&#8221;) skills, and during the final personal interviews they evaluate &#8220;soft&#8221; skills such as for example: Communication skills, Learning abilities, Teamwork capabilities or adaptability to work under stress to decide who to finally contract. I would like to end with what I believe each of us can do to have more employability and opportunities to find a new job. So, let me share here my three final tips for efficient Supply Chain Talent Searching: 1. Find your own &#8220;differential value&#8221; as a candidate, knowing the real market value of the skills you can bring to a company2. Create, maintain and care for an excellent network of professional contacts, which will allow you to open doors that are probably closed for other competitor candidates3. Ensure to have proper training in essential technical skills for each position to which you&#8217;re applying. In any case advanced English knowledge and advanced spreadsheets management, are both essential for any Supply Chain professional. Finally, when having any doubt about which should be the first step, the best advice I can give you, is to ask for expert advice.</p>\n<h3><strong>About The Author:</strong></h3>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.linkedin.com/in/miquelserracanta/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer nofollow\">Miquel Serracanta</a> is a business advisor, focused on Supply Chain, by serving the global supply chain community in optimizing End-to-End Supply Chains. Our services include Organization, Talent development (Head-hunting, Trainings, Kaizen events, Workshops, Team activities), Strategy design &amp; implementation, Planning (S&amp;OP, IBP) Projects &amp; Processes continuous improvement and all SC functions performance improvement in a synchronized way: Procurement, Logistics, Transportation, Warehousing, Distribution, Last Mile, Customer Service.</p>\n<p>&nbsp;</p>\n",
    "categories": [5458, 5702],

    "uuid": "bf54c3d2-2e64-4eca-a9c9-f6937c35e162",
    "post_id": 3841,
    "type": "blogs",
    "title": "Racing With the Machine:  Is your Supply Chain Job in Peril?",
    "slug": "racing-with-the-machine-is-your-supply-chain-job-in-peril",
    "date": "2020-09-08T15:57:10",
    "summary": null,
    "main_points": null,
    "recent_news": null,
    "related_articles": [],
    "web_content": "<p><strong>At the release of the white paper on the benefits of Robotic Process Automation (RPA) released by The Logistics &amp; Supply Chain Management Society and Automation Anywhere on 27<sup>th</sup> August , it was highlighted that Small to medium-sized forwarders and logistics providers are failing to reap all the productivity benefits of robotic process automation (RPA), according to one of the world’s leading logistics experts.</strong></p>\n<p>Professor Richard Wilding OBE, of Cranfield University, in the UK, said that most small and medium-sized enterprises (SME) in the forwarding and logistics sector could free up resources and reduce costs by automating basic, repetitive processes.</p>\n<h2><strong>Repetitive processes are a waste</strong></h2>\n<p style=\"vertical-align: baseline; margin: 0in 0in 7.5pt 0in;\"><span lang=\"EN-SG\" style=\"font-size: 10.5pt; font-family: 'Arial',sans-serif; color: #333333;\">Companies should identify any processes that are repetitive in nature, document the process and look at how RPA can be applied to automate the task, he said in a response to a question raised by co-host and leading supply chain expert, Dr. Raymon Krishnan.</span></p>\n<p style=\"margin: 0in; vertical-align: baseline;\"><span lang=\"EN-SG\" style=\"font-size: 10.5pt; font-family: 'Arial',sans-serif; color: #333333;\">“One of the key things in implementing [RPA] is to get everybody in the business to actually think about the types of processes they&#8217;re undertaking,” he told the press during a press briefing organised by LogiSYM.</span></p>\n<p style=\"vertical-align: baseline; margin: 0in 0in 7.5pt 0in;\"><span lang=\"EN-SG\" style=\"font-size: 10.5pt; font-family: 'Arial',sans-serif; color: #333333;\">“If you’re an SME, have a workshop and identify all those repetitive rules-based processes that you’re undertaking because that can help identify particular things which are going on within your organization which you can start applying [robotic process automation] technologies to.”</span></p>\n<p style=\"vertical-align: baseline; margin: 0in 0in 7.5pt 0in;\"><span lang=\"EN-SG\" style=\"font-size: 10.5pt; font-family: 'Arial',sans-serif; color: #333333;\">Wilding continued: “These repetitive processes are a waste. If you have to do the same thing over and over again, that&#8217;s a waste of resource within your businesses.</span></p>\n<p style=\"vertical-align: baseline; margin: 0in 0in 7.5pt 0in;\"><span lang=\"EN-SG\" style=\"font-size: 10.5pt; font-family: 'Arial',sans-serif; color: #333333;\">“We can use some of the lessons from &#8216;Just In Time&#8217; thinking for improving businesses, which we were all so good at and actually apply them now, but to repetitive processes.”</span></p>\n<p style=\"vertical-align: baseline; margin: 0in 0in 7.5pt 0in;\"><span lang=\"EN-SG\" style=\"font-size: 10.5pt; font-family: 'Arial',sans-serif; color: #333333;\">RPA technologies are already deployed by leading 3PLs to manage multiple processes including  inventory and freight management, returns and refunds processing and invoice management.</span></p>\n<p style=\"vertical-align: baseline; margin: 0in 0in 7.5pt 0in;\"><span lang=\"EN-SG\" style=\"font-size: 10.5pt; font-family: 'Arial',sans-serif; color: #333333;\">According to Wilding, one common process deficiency in SME logistics firms is the failure to fully integrate systems. “It could be that you’ve got these two[systems] that don&#8217;t talk to each other and you have somebody sitting there being a robot, taking data from one and applying it to the other,” he said. “If so, look to your IT department or get support from another organisation to join these things together. This is a real opportunity.”</span></p>\n<p style=\"vertical-align: baseline; margin: 0in 0in 7.5pt 0in;\"><span lang=\"EN-SG\" style=\"font-size: 10.5pt; font-family: 'Arial',sans-serif; color: #333333;\">Also speaking at the press briefing was Serene Keng, senior director for ASEAN, at Automation Anywhere, who said that for many companies,  the business area that typically comes out top in terms of automation potential is finance.</span></p>\n<p style=\"margin: 0in; vertical-align: baseline;\"><span lang=\"EN-SG\" style=\"font-size: 10.5pt; font-family: 'Arial',sans-serif; color: #333333;\">“Approximately 75% of processes in finance potentially can be automated because they are rule-based,” she explained. “Somebody has made a decision, it’s documented somewhere and therefore you don&#8217;t really need to have discretionary parameters to execute. So finance is a great hunting ground for processes to start automating.”</span></p>\n<h2><strong>Acceleration in RPA adoption</strong></h2>\n<p style=\"vertical-align: baseline; margin: 0in 0in 7.5pt 0in;\"><span lang=\"EN-SG\" style=\"font-size: 10.5pt; font-family: 'Arial',sans-serif; color: #333333;\">Covid lockdowns, which have forced employees to work from home, have accelerated RPA adoption across industries as managers have sought out new digital work processes, Wilding noted.</span></p>\n<p style=\"vertical-align: baseline; margin: 0in 0in 7.5pt 0in;\"><span lang=\"EN-SG\" style=\"font-size: 10.5pt; font-family: 'Arial',sans-serif; color: #333333;\">“When I&#8217;m talking to companies they are saying, ‘We were told by IT that it would take two years to implement that particular thing’. But now they&#8217;ve suddenly found out it took three weeks because necessity is the mother of invention. So what we’re finding is that people are looking at these things and saying, ‘We can do this’.</span></p>\n<p style=\"vertical-align: baseline; margin: 0in 0in 7.5pt 0in;\"><span lang=\"EN-SG\" style=\"font-size: 10.5pt; font-family: 'Arial',sans-serif; color: #333333;\">“I’m talking to big companies with thousands and thousands of employees [which are now implementing better] payroll processes, for example, and what they&#8217;re finding is they are getting a 20% [productivity gain] in the way people are working.</span></p>\n<p style=\"vertical-align: baseline; margin: 0in 0in 7.5pt 0in;\"><span lang=\"EN-SG\" style=\"font-size: 10.5pt; font-family: 'Arial',sans-serif; color: #333333;\">“They&#8217;re working remotely and had to think differently about the processes and have now removed all the non-value adding activity.”</span></p>\n<p style=\"vertical-align: baseline; margin: 0in 0in 7.5pt 0in;\"><span lang=\"EN-SG\" style=\"font-size: 10.5pt; font-family: 'Arial',sans-serif; color: #333333;\">Keng added that Covid-19 lockdowns had shined a light on the process weaknesses of many companies.</span></p>\n<p style=\"vertical-align: baseline; margin: 0in 0in 7.5pt 0in;\"><span lang=\"EN-SG\" style=\"font-size: 10.5pt; font-family: 'Arial',sans-serif; color: #333333;\">“It has shown that there a lot of events that can actually be done by muscle memory &#8211; by a something, rather than a someone.”</span></p>\n<h2><strong>About LogiSYM</strong></h2>\n<p>LogiSYM is the collaborative platform of The Logistics &amp; Supply Chain Management Society and engages the industry through its collaborative platforms, LogiSYM and CargoNOW.</p>\n<p>Practically all areas of the Logistics spectrum are represented and connected. Shippers, Freight Forwarders, Academics, Students, Carriers, Personal Effects Movers and other individuals and organisations form the core of our network of more than 100,000 Logisticians.</p>\n<p>With an emphasis on commercial experience and expertise LogiSYM is the leading community for the development of Logistics in the region and work with our members, government, organisations and professionals in raising the profile and expertise through a range of activities.</p>\n<p>LogiSYM has the proven history, framework, value for money and strategic reach to make it the right choice for you.</p>\n<ul>\n<li>To promote professional development of Logistics and Supply Chain Management;</li>\n<li>To serve as a resource centre for parties interested in Logistics and Supply Chain Management;</li>\n</ul>\n<h2><strong>About Automation Anywhere</strong></h2>\n<p>Automation Anywhere, a Robotic Process Automation (RPA) global market leader, empowers customers to automate end-to-end business processes with software robots that perform repetitive and manual tasks, resulting in dramatic productivity gains and business resiliency with less than a one-year payback, on average.</p>\n<p>The company offers the industry’s only cloud-native and web-based intelligent automation platform combining RPA, artificial intelligence, machine learning and analytics right out of the box, to help organizations rapidly start and scale their process automation journey. Its Bot Store is the world&#8217;s first and largest marketplace with more than 950 pre-built, intelligent automation solutions. With a global network of 1,900 partners, Automation Anywhere has deployed over 2.1 million bots in more than 90 countries to support the world&#8217;s largest enterprises, governments, and SMBs, including 85% of the top banks and ﬁnancial services companies, 90% of the top healthcare companies, 85% of the top technology companies, and 80% of the top telecom companies.</p>\n",
